+def _readability_extract(html: str) -> str:
+    """BB5-C05 (#1177): readability-lxml fallback extractor. trafilatura returns
+    empty trees on 30-50% of fetched pages; readability's article-detection
+    recovers many of them. Guarded import (skip-with-log when the optional dep
+    is absent — never break `_strip_html`). Returns extracted plain text or ""."""
+    if not html:

+        from readability import Document  # type: ignore
+    except ImportError:
+        logger.debug(
+            "[live_retriever] BB5-C05 readability-lxml not installed — "
+            "skipping fallback extractor"
+        )

+    try:
+        summary_html = Document(html).summary(html_partial=True)
+    except Exception as exc:  # noqa: BLE001 — readability runs lxml; a parse
+        # error must never break the strip path. (A C-level SIGSEGV would still
+        # escape, but readability only runs AFTER trafilatura already declined,
+        # and on the SAME doc that passed the trafilatura size gate.)

+        )

+    no_tags = re.sub(r"<[^>]+>", " ", summary_html or "")

+    return no_tags.strip()

+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+# BB5-S02 (#1177): cross-THREAD in-flight bypass-worker bound + leak gauge.
+#
+# `live_retriever._fetch_content` runs each `AccessBypass.fetch_with_bypass`
+# on a fresh daemon thread with its OWN `asyncio.run` loop, joined with a hard
+# timeout. On timeout the thread is ABANDONED (it keeps running, holding a live
+# Crawl4AI/Playwright browser subprocess mid-`arun`). Under the ~740-URL
+# benchmark fan-out, hundreds of abandoned threads + browser subprocesses
+# accumulate (the resource-exhaustion / segfault mechanism).
+#
+# `_get_crawl4ai_semaphore()` cannot bound this: it is lazy-bound to the
+# RUNNING loop, and every bypass worker thread has its OWN fresh loop — so it
+# only caps browsers WITHIN one thread. A `threading`-level BoundedSemaphore is
+# the only primitive that bounds the abandoned-thread FLEET across loops.
+#
+# Acquire at the TOP of the worker (in `live_retriever`), release in THAT
+# worker's `finally` — never in the outer join path (releasing on abandonment
+# would over-release; not releasing would leak the slot). Sized BELOW the
+# parallel `max_workers` so it creates back-pressure; no deadlock because the
+# inner per-backend wall-clocks guarantee every abandoned worker eventually
+# terminates and releases its slot.
+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+
+# Default ceiling on concurrently-LIVE bypass worker threads (each may hold a
+# browser subprocess). Env-overridable. Below the live_retriever parallel
+# `max_workers` ceiling (48) so abandoned in-flight workers cannot fan out a
+# browser-per-candidate. Named constant (LAW VI — no magic numbers).
+_BYPASS_INFLIGHT_DEFAULT_LIMIT = 16
+PG_BYPASS_MAX_INFLIGHT_ENV = "PG_BYPASS_MAX_INFLIGHT"
+
+_bypass_inflight_semaphore: "threading.BoundedSemaphore | None" = None
+_bypass_inflight_semaphore_lock = threading.Lock()
+
+# BB5-S02 leaked-worker gauge: monotonically-incremented count of bypass worker
+# threads that were ABANDONED (outer join timed out while the worker was still
+# alive). A non-zero gauge is the auditable signal that orphan browser
+# subprocesses may have accumulated. Guarded by its own lock.
+_bypass_leaked_worker_count: int = 0
+_bypass_leaked_worker_lock = threading.Lock()
+
+
+def _get_bypass_inflight_semaphore() -> "threading.BoundedSemaphore":
+    """BB5-S02 (#1177): lazy-init the cross-thread in-flight bypass-worker
+    bound. A `threading.BoundedSemaphore` (NOT asyncio) — it must bound worker
+    threads across their independent per-thread event loops.
+
+    Limit from `PG_BYPASS_MAX_INFLIGHT` (positive int), else
+    `_BYPASS_INFLIGHT_DEFAULT_LIMIT`. A malformed/<=0 value falls back to the
+    default — a bad knob must never disable the bound (which would re-open the
+    abandoned-fleet leak)."""
+    global _bypass_inflight_semaphore
+    if _bypass_inflight_semaphore is None:
+        with _bypass_inflight_semaphore_lock:
+            if _bypass_inflight_semaphore is None:
+                raw = os.getenv(PG_BYPASS_MAX_INFLIGHT_ENV)
+                limit = _BYPASS_INFLIGHT_DEFAULT_LIMIT
+                if raw is not None and raw.strip():
+                    try:
+                        parsed = int(raw)
+                        if parsed > 0:
+                            limit = parsed
+                    except ValueError:
+                        limit = _BYPASS_INFLIGHT_DEFAULT_LIMIT
+                _bypass_inflight_semaphore = threading.BoundedSemaphore(limit)
+    return _bypass_inflight_semaphore
+
+
+def record_bypass_leaked_worker() -> int:
+    """BB5-S02 (#1177): increment + return the leaked-bypass-worker gauge. The
+    caller (live_retriever) invokes this when an outer fetch join times out
+    while the worker thread is still alive (abandoned → potential orphan
+    browser subprocess). Thread-safe; returns the new total for logging."""
+    global _bypass_leaked_worker_count
+    with _bypass_leaked_worker_lock:
+        _bypass_leaked_worker_count += 1
+        return _bypass_leaked_worker_count
+
+
+def bypass_leaked_worker_count() -> int:
+    """BB5-S02 (#1177): read the current leaked-bypass-worker gauge (auditable
+    orphan-subprocess signal). Thread-safe snapshot."""
+    with _bypass_leaked_worker_lock:
+        return _bypass_leaked_worker_count
+
+
+def reset_bypass_leak_state() -> None:
+    """BB5-S02 (#1177): reset the leak gauge + in-flight semaphore. For test
+    isolation ONLY — not called on the production path."""
+    global _bypass_leaked_worker_count, _bypass_inflight_semaphore
+    with _bypass_leaked_worker_lock:
+        _bypass_leaked_worker_count = 0
+    with _bypass_inflight_semaphore_lock:
+        _bypass_inflight_semaphore = None
+
+
+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+# BB5-S03 (#1177): SIGSEGV-mitigated shared trafilatura extractor.
+#
+# `trafilatura.extract` runs libxml2 (a C extension). On a pathological /
+# malformed / adversarial document libxml2 can SIGSEGV (drb_76 exit 139) — a
+# C-level crash that is NOT a Python exception and CANNOT be caught by
+# `except Exception`. A try/except around the call is false confidence.
+#
+# True containment is a per-page hard-killable subprocess, but that is heavy at
+# hundreds of calls/run AND `resource` RLIMIT is Unix-only (no-op on win32).
+# So the DEFAULT is lean MITIGATION (not containment): size-bound the HTML and
+# prefer the caller's regex fallback for oversized/suspect docs, which never
+# enters libxml2 at all. An optional hard-killable subprocess path is gated
+# behind `PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS=1` (OFF by default).
+#
+# Lives in access_bypass (NOT live_retriever): live_retriever already imports
+# access_bypass, so the reverse import would be circular. Both trafilatura
+# sites import this one guarded entrypoint.
+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+
+# Upper bound (chars) on HTML handed to libxml2 via trafilatura. A document
+# larger than this is treated as suspect/oversized: we skip trafilatura and
+# signal the caller to use its regex fallback (which never enters the C
+# extension). Env-overridable. Named constant (LAW VI).
+_TRAFILATURA_MAX_HTML_CHARS = int(
+    os.getenv("PG_TRAFILATURA_MAX_HTML_CHARS", "3000000")
+)
+PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS_ENV = "PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS"
+# Hard wall-clock for the optional subprocess extractor path (seconds).
+_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS_TIMEOUT = float(
+    os.getenv("PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS_TIMEOUT_SECONDS", "20")
+)
+
+
+def _html_is_extract_safe(html: str) -> bool:
+    """BB5-S03 (#1177): cheap pre-validation gate. Returns False for an
+    oversized document (over `_TRAFILATURA_MAX_HTML_CHARS`) that should bypass
+    libxml2 entirely. Pure size check — no parsing, never itself crashes."""
+    if not html:
+        return False
+    if len(html) > _TRAFILATURA_MAX_HTML_CHARS:
+        return False
+    return True
+
+
+def _trafilatura_extract_subprocess(html: str, **kwargs: Any) -> "str | None":
+    """BB5-S03 (#1177): run `trafilatura.extract` in a hard-killable child
+    process so a libxml2 SIGSEGV takes down the child (exit 139) instead of the
+    sweep. Returns the extracted text, or None on timeout/crash/error.
+
+    Gated OFF by default (`PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS=1` to enable) — true
+    containment is heavy at hundreds of calls/run. Best-effort: any failure
+    (spawn error, non-zero exit incl. -11/139 SIGSEGV, timeout) returns None so
+    the caller falls back to regex extraction. Never raises."""
+    import json
+    import subprocess
+
+    payload = json.dumps({"html": html, "kwargs": kwargs})
+    code = (
+        "import sys, json\n"
+        "data = json.loads(sys.stdin.read())\n"
+        "import trafilatura\n"
+        "out = trafilatura.extract(data['html'], **data['kwargs']) or ''\n"
+        "sys.stdout.write(out)\n"
+    )
+    try:
+        proc = subprocess.run(
+            [sys.executable, "-c", code],
+            input=payload,
+            capture_output=True,
+            text=True,
+            timeout=_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS_TIMEOUT,
+        )
+    except (subprocess.TimeoutExpired, OSError, ValueError) as exc:
+        logger.warning(
+            "[ACCESS] BB5-S03 trafilatura subprocess failed (%s) — "
+            "regex fallback", type(exc).__name__,
+        )
+        return None
+    if proc.returncode != 0:
+        # A negative return code is a signal (e.g. -11 == SIGSEGV / exit 139):
+        # the child crashed on a pathological doc and the SWEEP survived.
+        logger.warning(
+            "[ACCESS] BB5-S03 trafilatura subprocess exited rc=%s "
+            "(SIGSEGV-class crash contained) — regex fallback",
+            proc.returncode,
+        )
+        return None
+    return proc.stdout or None
+
+
+def safe_trafilatura_extract(html: str, **kwargs: Any) -> "str | None":
+    """BB5-S03 (#1177): the ONE guarded trafilatura entrypoint used by every
+    extraction site (live_retriever `_strip_html`, access_bypass
+    `_try_crawl4ai`).
+
+    Contract:
+      - Returns extracted text (str) on success, or None when extraction is
+        unsafe/empty/failed (caller falls back to its own regex path).
+      - Honest MITIGATION, not containment, on the default in-process path:
+        an oversized/suspect doc skips libxml2 (returns None → regex fallback);
+        a SIGSEGV on a doc that passes the size gate is still uncatchable
+        in-process. Enable `PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS=1` for true containment.
+      - Never raises (the C-extension SIGSEGV is the one thing it cannot
+        promise to catch on the in-process path — documented, not hidden)."""
+    if not _html_is_extract_safe(html):
+        return None
+    if os.getenv(PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS_ENV, "0") == "1":
+        return _trafilatura_extract_subprocess(html, **kwargs)
+    try:
+        import trafilatura  # type: ignore
+        return trafilatura.extract(html, **kwargs) or None
+    except Exception as exc:  # noqa: BLE001 — Python-level errors only; a
+        # libxml2 SIGSEGV is NOT a Python exception and escapes this guard (by
+        # design — that is what PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS=1 contains).
+        logger.debug(
+            "[ACCESS] BB5-S03 trafilatura in-process extract error (%s) — "
+            "regex fallback", type(exc).__name__,
+        )
+        return None
+

+OFFLINE deterministic coverage (no network, no spend, no real browser) for:
+
+  - BB5-S02 — abandoned-bypass-worker teardown: a cross-THREAD BoundedSemaphore
+    bounds concurrently-LIVE bypass workers across their independent per-thread
+    event loops; the slot is released in the worker's OWN finally (never the
+    outer join path); an abandoned worker increments a leaked-worker gauge; the
+    bound never deadlocks the sweep; `_bypass_worker` runs under the
+    wedged-task-draining `polaris_asyncio_run`.
+
+  - BB5-S03 — SIGSEGV-mitigated trafilatura: the shared `safe_trafilatura_extract`
+    guard size-bounds the HTML (an oversized/suspect doc skips libxml2 and
+    returns None → caller's regex fallback), never raises, and the optional
+    subprocess path contains a SIGSEGV-class child crash (returns None).
+
+  - BB5-C05 — extractor fallback chain + distinct telemetry: `_strip_html` falls
+    back to readability-lxml when trafilatura returns an empty tree; a fetch that
+    returns a real 200 body but whose extractor chain collapses below the floor
+    is surfaced as the DISTINCT "fetched_200_but_empty_extract" telemetry bucket
+    (not a silent generic miss).
+
+All tests monkeypatch the network/extractor boundary; none hit the wire.
+"""
+
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import threading
+import time
+from dataclasses import dataclass
+from typing import Any
+
+import pytest
+
+import src.tools.access_bypass as ab
+from src.polaris_graph.retrieval import live_retriever
+
+
+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+# Fakes
+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+

+@dataclass
+class _FakeAccessResult:
+    success: bool = True
+    content: str = "fake markdown content with real research words here"
+    access_method: str = "crawl4ai"
+    metadata: dict | None = None
+
+
+@pytest.fixture(autouse=True)
+def _reset_bypass_leak_state():
+    """Isolate the module-level S02 gauge + semaphore between tests."""
+    ab.reset_bypass_leak_state()
+    yield
+    ab.reset_bypass_leak_state()
+

+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+# BB5-S02 — cross-thread in-flight bound + leak gauge
+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+
+
+def test_inflight_semaphore_is_cross_thread_bounded_semaphore(monkeypatch):
+    """The in-flight bound is a threading.BoundedSemaphore (NOT asyncio) sized
+    from PG_BYPASS_MAX_INFLIGHT — it must bound worker THREADS across loops."""
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_BYPASS_MAX_INFLIGHT", "3")
+    ab.reset_bypass_leak_state()  # force re-read of the env knob
+    sem = ab._get_bypass_inflight_semaphore()
+    assert isinstance(sem, threading.BoundedSemaphore)
+    # Acquire up to the limit; the 4th non-blocking acquire must fail.
+    assert sem.acquire(blocking=False) is True
+    assert sem.acquire(blocking=False) is True
+    assert sem.acquire(blocking=False) is True
+    assert sem.acquire(blocking=False) is False
+    sem.release()
+    sem.release()
+    sem.release()
+
+
+def test_malformed_inflight_env_falls_back_to_default(monkeypatch):
+    """A bad PG_BYPASS_MAX_INFLIGHT must NOT disable the bound (would re-open
+    the abandoned-fleet leak) — it falls back to the named default."""
+    for bad in ("not-an-int", "0", "-5", ""):
+        monkeypatch.setenv("PG_BYPASS_MAX_INFLIGHT", bad)
+        ab.reset_bypass_leak_state()
+        sem = ab._get_bypass_inflight_semaphore()
+        # Default limit acquirable exactly _BYPASS_INFLIGHT_DEFAULT_LIMIT times.
+        got = 0
+        while sem.acquire(blocking=False):
+            got += 1
+            if got > ab._BYPASS_INFLIGHT_DEFAULT_LIMIT + 5:
+                break
+        assert got == ab._BYPASS_INFLIGHT_DEFAULT_LIMIT
+        for _ in range(got):
+            sem.release()
+
+
+def test_leaked_worker_gauge_increments_and_reads(monkeypatch):
+    """record_bypass_leaked_worker bumps the auditable orphan-subprocess gauge;
+    bypass_leaked_worker_count reads it; reset clears it."""
+    assert ab.bypass_leaked_worker_count() == 0
+    assert ab.record_bypass_leaked_worker() == 1
+    assert ab.record_bypass_leaked_worker() == 2
+    assert ab.bypass_leaked_worker_count() == 2
+    ab.reset_bypass_leak_state()
+    assert ab.bypass_leaked_worker_count() == 0
+

+def test_abandoned_worker_increments_leak_gauge(monkeypatch):
+    """A bypass worker that out-runs the join deadline is abandoned → the leak
+    gauge increments AND the call falls back to naive httpx (does not hang)."""
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_DISABLE_ACCESS_BYPASS", "0")
+    # Tiny join deadline so the slow worker is guaranteed to be abandoned.
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_FETCH_DEADLINE_SECONDS", "0.3")
+
+    class _SlowBypass:
+        async def fetch_with_bypass(self, url, prefer_legal=True):
+            import asyncio
+            await asyncio.sleep(5.0)  # outlives the 0.3s join deadline
+            return _FakeAccessResult()
+
+    monkeypatch.setattr(ab, "AccessBypass", _SlowBypass)
+    # Make the naive fallback deterministic + offline.
+    monkeypatch.setattr(
+        live_retriever, "_fallback_naive_fetch",
+        lambda url, mc, t0, reason: ("", False, "", "", ""),
+    )
+
+    assert ab.bypass_leaked_worker_count() == 0
+    content, ok, _t, _b, _j = live_retriever._fetch_content(
+        "https://example.com/slow", max_chars=1000,
+    )
+    assert ok is False  # fell back to the (stubbed) naive path
+    assert ab.bypass_leaked_worker_count() == 1
+

+def test_bypass_worker_uses_polaris_asyncio_run(monkeypatch):
+    """BB5-S02: the worker must run under polaris_asyncio_run (wedged-task
+    drain), NOT bare asyncio.run — assert the drain-runner is invoked."""
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_DISABLE_ACCESS_BYPASS", "0")
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_FETCH_DEADLINE_SECONDS", "30")
+
+    called = {"polaris_run": 0}
+    real_runner = ab.polaris_asyncio_run
+
+    def _spy_runner(coro):
+        called["polaris_run"] += 1
+        return real_runner(coro)
+
+    monkeypatch.setattr(ab, "polaris_asyncio_run", _spy_runner)
+
+    class _FastBypass:
+        async def fetch_with_bypass(self, url, prefer_legal=True):
+            return _FakeAccessResult()
+
+    monkeypatch.setattr(ab, "AccessBypass", _FastBypass)
+
+    content, ok, _t, _b, _j = live_retriever._fetch_content(
+        "https://example.com/fast", max_chars=1000,
+    )
+    assert ok is True
+    assert "fake markdown content" in content
+    assert called["polaris_run"] == 1
+
+
+def test_inflight_bound_does_not_deadlock_under_contention(monkeypatch):
+    """No-deadlock property: with the slot limit far BELOW the number of
+    workers, every worker still eventually acquires + releases (the inner
+    wall-clock guarantees termination) — the batch drains in bounded time."""
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_BYPASS_MAX_INFLIGHT", "2")
+    ab.reset_bypass_leak_state()
+    sem = ab._get_bypass_inflight_semaphore()
+
+    live_peak = {"max": 0}
+    live_now = {"n": 0}
+    lock = threading.Lock()
+    done = {"n": 0}
+
+    def _worker():
+        sem.acquire()
+        try:
+            with lock:
+                live_now["n"] += 1
+                live_peak["max"] = max(live_peak["max"], live_now["n"])
+            time.sleep(0.02)  # simulate in-flight fetch
+        finally:
+            with lock:
+                live_now["n"] -= 1
+                done["n"] += 1
+            sem.release()
+
+    threads = [threading.Thread(target=_worker) for _ in range(20)]
+    start = time.monotonic()
+    for t in threads:
+        t.start()
+    for t in threads:
+        t.join(timeout=10.0)
+    elapsed = time.monotonic() - start
+
+    assert done["n"] == 20, "every worker must finish (no deadlock)"
+    assert live_peak["max"] <= 2, "in-flight concurrency must respect the bound"
+    assert elapsed < 10.0
+
+
+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+# BB5-S03 — SIGSEGV-mitigated trafilatura guard
+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+
+
+def test_safe_trafilatura_skips_oversized_html(monkeypatch):
+    """An oversized doc (over the size gate) must bypass libxml2 entirely →
+    returns None so the caller uses its regex fallback. Asserts trafilatura is
+    never even called for the oversized input. (The char-cap is a module-level
+    deploy-slate constant read at import, so patch it directly here.)"""
+    monkeypatch.setattr(ab, "_TRAFILATURA_MAX_HTML_CHARS", 1000)
+    monkeypatch.delenv("PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS", raising=False)
+
+    # If trafilatura WERE called we'd see this flag flip.
+    import trafilatura
+    called = {"n": 0}
+    monkeypatch.setattr(
+        trafilatura, "extract",
+        lambda *a, **k: (called.__setitem__("n", called["n"] + 1) or "x"),
+    )
+
+    oversized = "<p>" + ("x" * 5000) + "</p>"
+    assert ab.safe_trafilatura_extract(oversized) is None
+    assert called["n"] == 0, "oversized HTML must never reach libxml2"
+
+
+def test_safe_trafilatura_in_process_returns_extracted(monkeypatch):
+    """In-process path returns trafilatura's text when the doc is within the
+    size gate (default 3M chars) and extraction succeeds."""
+    monkeypatch.delenv("PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS", raising=False)
+    import trafilatura
+    monkeypatch.setattr(trafilatura, "extract", lambda *a, **k: "clean body text")
+    assert ab.safe_trafilatura_extract("<p>hi</p>") == "clean body text"
+
+
+def test_safe_trafilatura_never_raises_on_python_error(monkeypatch):
+    """A Python-level extract error returns None (regex fallback), never raises."""
+    monkeypatch.delenv("PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS", raising=False)
+    import trafilatura
+
+    def _boom(*a, **k):
+        raise ValueError("malformed doc")
+
+    monkeypatch.setattr(trafilatura, "extract", _boom)
+    assert ab.safe_trafilatura_extract("<p>hi</p>") is None
+
+
+def test_safe_trafilatura_subprocess_contains_sigsegv(monkeypatch):
+    """The optional subprocess path contains a SIGSEGV-class child crash: a
+    negative/non-zero return code → None (caller falls back), sweep survives."""
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS", "1")
+
+    @dataclass
+    class _CrashedProc:
+        returncode: int = -11  # SIGSEGV == exit 139
+        stdout: str = ""
+        stderr: str = ""
+
+    import subprocess
+    monkeypatch.setattr(subprocess, "run", lambda *a, **k: _CrashedProc())
+    # Must not raise; returns None so the caller uses its regex fallback.
+    assert ab.safe_trafilatura_extract("<p>pathological</p>") is None
+
+
+def test_safe_trafilatura_subprocess_timeout_returns_none(monkeypatch):
+    """A subprocess timeout is contained (None), never propagated."""
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS", "1")
+    import subprocess
+
+    def _timeout(*a, **k):
+        raise subprocess.TimeoutExpired(cmd="x", timeout=1)
+
+    monkeypatch.setattr(subprocess, "run", _timeout)
+    assert ab.safe_trafilatura_extract("<p>slow</p>") is None
+
+
+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+# BB5-C05 — extractor fallback chain + distinct telemetry
+# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
+
+
+def test_strip_html_falls_back_to_readability(monkeypatch):
+    """When trafilatura returns empty, _strip_html tries readability-lxml before
+    the last-resort regex strip."""
+    # safe_trafilatura_extract returns None (empty tree).
+    monkeypatch.setattr(ab, "safe_trafilatura_extract", lambda *a, **k: None)
+    monkeypatch.setattr(
+        live_retriever, "_readability_extract",
+        lambda html: "readability recovered article body",
+    )
+    # Disable table append so we read the base extractor result directly.
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_FETCH_TABLE_LINEARIZE", "0")
+    out = live_retriever._strip_html("<html><body><p>x</p></body></html>")
+    assert out == "readability recovered article body"
+
+
+def test_strip_html_regex_last_resort_when_both_empty(monkeypatch):
+    """When trafilatura AND readability both yield nothing, the regex strip is
+    the final fallback (never returns empty for real tag soup)."""
+    monkeypatch.setattr(ab, "safe_trafilatura_extract", lambda *a, **k: None)
+    monkeypatch.setattr(live_retriever, "_readability_extract", lambda html: "")
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_FETCH_TABLE_LINEARIZE", "0")
+    out = live_retriever._strip_html(
+        "<html><body><p>plain visible words survive</p></body></html>"
+    )
+    assert "plain visible words survive" in out
+
+
+def test_readability_extract_missing_dep_is_skip_not_crash(monkeypatch):
+    """A missing readability-lxml dep logs + returns '' — never breaks strip."""
+    import builtins
+    real_import = builtins.__import__
+
+    def _no_readability(name, *args, **kwargs):
+        if name == "readability":
+            raise ImportError("readability-lxml not installed")
+        return real_import(name, *args, **kwargs)
+
+    monkeypatch.setattr(builtins, "__import__", _no_readability)
+    assert live_retriever._readability_extract("<p>x</p>") == ""
+
+
+def test_fetched_200_but_empty_extract_distinct_telemetry(monkeypatch):
+    """BB5-C05: a real 200 body that the extractor chain collapses below the
+    floor is surfaced as the DISTINCT 'fetched_200_but_empty_extract' bucket,
+    not a silent generic miss."""
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_DISABLE_ACCESS_BYPASS", "0")
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_FETCH_DEADLINE_SECONDS", "30")
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_FETCH_NONEMPTY_RAW_FLOOR", "200")
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_FETCH_EMPTY_EXTRACT_FLOOR", "50")
+
+    # Backend returns a big raw body...
+    big_raw = "<html>" + ("<div></div>" * 500) + "</html>"
+
+    class _BigEmptyBypass:
+        async def fetch_with_bypass(self, url, prefer_legal=True):
+            return _FakeAccessResult(success=True, content=big_raw)

+    monkeypatch.setattr(ab, "AccessBypass", _BigEmptyBypass)
+    # ...but the extractor chain yields nothing usable.
+    monkeypatch.setattr(live_retriever, "_strip_html", lambda c: "")
+
+    captured = {}
+    monkeypatch.setattr(
+        live_retriever, "_m45_record_fetch_telemetry",
+        lambda url, method, failure_reason="": captured.__setitem__(
+            "reason", failure_reason
+        ),
+    )
+
+    content, ok, _t, _b, _j = live_retriever._fetch_content(
+        "https://example.com/empty-extract", max_chars=25000,
+    )
+    assert len(big_raw) >= 200
+    assert content == ""
+    assert ok is False
+    assert captured.get("reason") == "fetched_200_but_empty_extract"
+
+
+def test_normal_fetch_not_flagged_as_empty_extract(monkeypatch):
+    """A healthy fetch (real extracted body) is NOT mislabelled as the empty
+    bucket — guards against a false-positive on the new branch."""

+    assert captured["reason"] == ""  # the OK telemetry path, not empty-extract

.\docs\credibility_adaptive_weighting_and_bothsides_recs_2026_06_08.md:1:# POLARIS Source-Credibility & Multi-Perspective Recommendations Report\n### Driving two revisions to `docs/credibility_weighted_sourcing_redesign_plan_2026_06_07.md` — LAYER 1 (scoring) and LAYER 6 (composition + UI)\n\n**Author:** Lead analyst (Claude). **Date:** 2026-06-08.\n**Inputs:** three research streams (per-question adaptive credibility weighting; neutral multi-perspective presentation; friendly UI/artifact patterns).\n**Status:** revision driver. Each layer below states what it **REPLACES** in the Codex-APPROVE'd 2026-06-07 plan, then the concrete mechanism, auditability, reliability, and POLARIS wiring.\n\n**Invariants preserved across both revisions** (these are not negotiable and the revisions do not weaken them): the LLM credibility-judge is **advisory only** — `strict_verify`'s six per-sentence checks (`provenance_generator.py:1156`) remain the binding faithfulness gate; every new layer is **flag-gated, default-OFF byte-identical**, fail-loud on missing inputs; weight is **evidence quality/tier, never headcount**; every displayed aggregate is **one click from the cited `[#ev:id:start-end]` span and its VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict**; the credibility prior stays **self-computed and verifier-overridable** (no single external rater hardwired); independence-collapse (`synthesis/independence_collapse.py`) still runs before any weighted tally; the contested-topic adjudication **reuses the existing 4-role / voter-arbiter pipeline** (`roles/role_pipeline.py` + `honest_sweep_integration.py`), open-weight voters only — no parallel path is built.\n\n---\n\n## 1. LAYER 1 (scoring): adaptive per-question credibility-skill, replacing the fixed domain-rubric selector\n\n### 1.1 What this REPLACES\n\nThe 2026-06-07 plan's **Phase 2a/2b (L1)** selects one of **three fixed reliability rubrics** (clinical → RCT+peer-review+RoB; econ/policy → design-validity; qualitative → CERQual) keyed off the detected domain. That is still a small lookup table: domain → rubric. The operator constraint is explicit — **replace fixed domain rubrics** with a **generic, domain-agnostic credibility skill the LLM applies by reasoning per question**. Research stream #1's central finding is that the frontier (OpenAI, Gemini, Claude) has already moved this way, and that Perplexity's baked-in EEAT/domain-authority scoring is the closest-to-forbidden counter-example (gameable, popularity-biased, ~60% Google-overlap). We copy the reasoned-generic camp.\n\nThe revision: **domain stops being a selector and becomes context that primes one generic skill.** There is exactly one credibility skill; the detected `scope_template` domain is passed in as a hint the skill reasons over ("this is a clinical efficacy question, so weight trial design and RoB heavily"), not a branch that swaps rubrics. This scales to 10,000+ fields with zero per-field config.\n\n### 1.2 The exact mechanism — credibility-skill / guardrail prompt × (reliability × relevance)\n\n**Step A — deterministic signals (POLARIS produces these; unchanged substrate).** `authority_model.score_source_authority` and `tier_classifier` already emit, per source, the field-agnostic primitives: `authority_score [0,1]`, `source_class`, `corroboration_count` (independent-host agreement), `authority_confidence`, `signal_scores` (the A–E sub-scores), plus `junk_class` / `predatory_oa` (`source_class.py:71-89`). Independence-collapse (`independence_collapse.py`) emits `origin_cluster_id` + canonical-origin designation + copy flag. **None of this is replaced.** These are the inspectable, host-name-free, self-computed inputs (LAW VI: zero host literals in code).\n\n**Step B — the credibility skill consumes those signals and weights them per question.** A new pure prompt module, `authority/credibility_skill.py`, runs a **JudgeRank-style 3-step decomposition** (arXiv 2411.00142) — chosen because each step is inspectable text and is itself the audit template:\n\n1. **Query analysis** — identify what THIS question actually needs (the claim type, what would count as strong evidence for it).\n2. **Source analysis** — for each candidate source, a query-AWARE assessment applying **generic SIFT + lateral-reading + provenance heuristics**, NOT a domain table. The skill's instruction block encodes the domain-agnostic primacy heuristics that are OpenAI's own deep-research pattern: *prefer the primary/official source over an aggregator or SEO blog; prefer the original paper over a survey/secondary summary; corroborate laterally (does independent coverage agree); weigh source incentives/track record; downgrade stale-but-authoritative and retracted/superseded* (the latter wires to the existing `supersession.py` Phase 3 signal).\n3. **Two-axis judgment with rationale** — emit, per source, **RELIABILITY × RELEVANCE** (the EFSA/OHAT weight-of-evidence two-axis, which POLARIS currently conflates into one tier): reliability = internal validity/method given what the skill read in the signals; relevance = directness to this specific question. The product is the per-question credibility weight. **Crucially, the skill is told its priors are the `authority_model` signals and that it may up- or down-weight them with a stated reason** — it does not invent authority from nothing, and it cannot silently override `authority_confidence=LOW` into a fabricated HIGH (thin OpenAlex/ROR signal stays honestly LOW).\n\n**Output schema (machine-parseable, bound to the schema discipline already in §8.3.9):** per source — `{reliability_score, relevance_score, credibility_weight, rationale_string, signals_cited:[...]}`. The weight is **a visible, revisable rationale string, never a hidden scalar and never a fine-tuned-in behavior** (this is why we reject the CAG fine-tune approach from stream #1: opaque learned weights are exactly the auditability failure POLARIS differentiates against — borrow CAG's *evidence* that credibility-conditioning gives noise robustness, and its three generic dimensions of relevance/timeliness/reliability, but implement them at inference time as a prompt-visible signal).\n\n### 1.3 How it stays AUDITABLE (auditable by construction, not bolted on)\n\nThe judgment IS a reasoning trace, so it is emitted verbatim and **bound to the same provenance substrate POLARIS already has**:\n\n- The per-source `credibility_weight` + `rationale_string` + `signals_cited` attach to the source's `AuthorityResult` as **additive fields** (mirroring how `signal_scores`, `junk_class`, `predatory_oa` are already additive side-outputs on the dataclass), emitted on rows in `tier_classifier.py`.\n- At claim time, the weight flows into the four Phase-1/Phase-8 disclosure fields on `SentenceVerification` (`credibility_weight`, `independent_origin_count`, `certainty_label`, `span_verdict`), so each verified sentence shows **which source was weighted how, and why**, one click from its `[#ev]` span.\n- Because the skill cites the deterministic `signals_cited` it reasoned from, the rationale is **checkable against the inputs** — a reviewer can confirm "preferred A over B because A is the primary trial-registry entry and B a secondary news summary" against the actual `source_class` values. The rationale is a **claim to verify, not ground truth** (post-hoc rationalization risk per stream #1) — so it is advisory and the binding gate stays `strict_verify`.\n\nThis is the §-1.1-compliant story: no metadata/count/string-presence signal, every weight traceable to a cited span and an inspectable reason.\n\n### 1.4 Reliability and where it fails (and the guardrail)\n\nStream #1 is blunt about the failure modes, and they bound the design: LLMs "treat all retrieved documents as equally valid" unless explicitly steered and over-rely on high-frequency claims (arXiv 2505.17762); AuthorityBench (2603.25092) shows authority perception is **inconsistent across domains and highly prompt-sensitive**, struggles with false authority, and exhibits position/verbosity/self-preference bias. Therefore:\n\n- **The skill is ADVISORY to ranking/selection, never the faithfulness gate.** It changes *which rows are billed/weighted*, not *whether a sentence verifies its span*. `strict_verify`, 4-role/two-family segregation, and the independent `corpus_approval_gate` tier-distribution backstop all still run sequentially.\n- **Bias mitigations baked into the prompt:** score rationale-first then number; randomize candidate order to blunt position bias; run pointwise (per-source) to avoid listwise permutation instability.\n- **Offline validation before trust:** the chosen judge model+prompt is validated on an **AuthorityBench-style harness** (authority-PERCEPTION only, per the §6a no-overstatement correction — not as a volume-vulnerability benchmark) plus the existing vax adversarial fixture, before it is allowed on the shipping path. Calibration (Brier/ECE) on the emitted weights runs in the existing Phase 11 harness.\n- **Capture resistance:** multi-signal, self-computed, verifier-overridable — no NewsGuard/MBFC/Ad Fontes verdict is hardwired as ground truth (the FTC-capture risk).\n\n### 1.5 The honest gap + exactly what POLARIS builds for L1\n\n**HAVE:** deterministic authority signals (`authority_model`, `tier_classifier`), the additive `AuthorityResult`/`SentenceVerification` schema, independence-collapse, `scope_templates` domain detection, the JSON-verdict schema discipline.\n**MISSING:** the generic per-question credibility skill itself, and the second (relevance) axis.\n**BUILD (revision to Phase 2a/2b):**\n1. `authority/credibility_skill.py` — the pure 3-step (query→source→two-axis-judgment) prompt module emitting `{reliability, relevance, credibility_weight, rationale, signals_cited}`. Domain is an input *hint*, not a rubric switch. (Replaces the fixed-rubric selector in `credibility_prior.py`.)\n2. Add `relevance_score` (and the rationale fields) to `AuthorityResult` (`source_class.py:75`); emit on rows in `tier_classifier.py`.\n3. Wire the skill's weight into the L5 weight-mass tally and the L7 disclosure fields — advisory input, not a gate.\n4. Flag-gated default-OFF byte-identical; OFF = the legacy single-scalar path, byte-for-byte.\n\n---\n\n## 2. LAYER 6 (composition + UI): neutral multi-perspective + transparent evidence-weight artifact, replacing the forewarning/fringe framing\n\n### 2.1 What this REPLACES\n\nThe 2026-06-07 plan's **Phase 7 (L6)** composes contested claims as "consensus at high weight + minority attributed at low weight **with explicit forewarning**, medical-misinfo **low-weight/fringe**, ABSTAIN over fabricated balance." The operator directive is to **replace the forewarning/fringe framing** with a **neutral multi-perspective presentation where competing world-views are shown as legitimate, each carrying its real (possibly asymmetric) evidence weight, and the user judges** — no bias, no stamps, no forewarning prose.\n\n### 2.2 The hard tension, named and resolved (do not skip this)\n\nThere is a real conflict between two binding constraints, and both sides have a lethal failure mode:\n\n- The operator wants **no fringe/forewarning stamp, all sides legitimate, no bias.**\n- The **clinical-safety invariant #5** (binding, preserved) plus Dixon-Clarke 2013 (PubMed 23193194, measured harm: falsely-balanced vaccine reporting *reduced* perceived safety and vaccination intent), Wikipedia FRINGE, and §-1.1 all say **equal treatment of unequal evidence is itself bias** and is "lethal in clinical." I am not authorized to drop invariant #5.\n\n**The reconciliation — handed to us nearly verbatim by all three streams: replace the LABEL with the BASIS.** Wikipedia NPOV's "neutral *editing*, not neutral *content*"; GRADE's "show the basis, let the user infer"; the no-warning rule from stream #2 is satisfiable **if and only if the criteria behind any weight are displayed**. So:\n\n- The **system** stamps nothing — no "fringe," no "debunked," no forewarning sentence. That is the neutrality.\n- The **evidence weight** carries the (often asymmetric) truth, rendered as a visible **per-perspective evidence-basis panel** the user reads and judges. The asymmetry — *14 RCTs + 3 systematic reviews [High]* vs *2 case reports + mechanistic argument [Very Low]* — becomes **visible in the artifact** instead of **asserted in a stamp**. The user infers; the system does not editorialize.\n- "Legitimate" means **shown with its real (possibly low) weight and one-click drill-down to span + verdict** — NOT "shown as equally supported." A genuine world-view dispute with no empirical consensus (values, forecasting) shows steelmanned sides at honest parity; an empirical dispute with consensus shows the real weight distribution.\n- The medical-misinfo case is handled **without the banned word**: its panel is simply **near-empty of independent high-tier basis**, and where there is no independent consensus the claim **ABSTAINs** ("contested; no independent consensus" — reusing existing refuse/unresolved behavior). This preserves invariant #5's *substance* (not normalized as an equal side) while dropping the stamp.\n\nThis is neutral AND anti-false-balance AND §-1.1-safe simultaneously — the operator's "let the user judge" satisfied by *showing the basis*, not by *equalizing the boxes*.\n\n### 2.3 The exact composition mechanism\n\nPer question, the composition path first **diagnoses the contestation type** (this IS the adaptive guardrail, copied from Anthropic's even-handedness "lack-of-consensus" discriminator + OpenAI's seek-the-truth-together):\n\n- **empirical-with-consensus** (vaccines, climate) → due-weight: each side shown, weight proportional to verified-evidence quality; the asymmetry is the message, carried by the basis panel.\n- **genuine-uncertainty** (open scientific questions) → separate *supported* from *open*; sides at honest parity.\n- **values dispute** (politics, ethics) → **steelman each legitimate view** (Ideological Turing Test, neutral terminology, no verdict); no evidence-weight asymmetry asserted because there is no due weight to defer to.\n- **forecasting** (AI-and-jobs) → scenario spread, projective not factual.\n\nEach perspective is gathered through its **own retrieval lens** (MODS-style per-perspective retrieval + citation, arXiv 2502.00322 — raw LLMs silently drop minority views; per-perspective retrieval prevents the drop), then composed via the **existing 4-role / voter-arbiter agreement** (cross-lineage, open-weight voters — the bridging/balanced-panel analog) — **not a new adjudication path**. Reranking-for-balance (arXiv 2506.15925) selects the most balanced faithful candidate, because direct just-prompt-balanced generation empirically skews. **The weight attached to each perspective is evidence QUALITY × independent-origin count, never document count** — else we rebuild Ground News's source-count bias inside the summarizer.\n\n### 2.4 The friendly UI artifact — design\n\nBuilt on the **components that already exist** (#744 citation chip + hover source card, #745 per-claim verdict chip, #747 Proof Replay split-view, #757 report page, #758 claim-anchored compare view) — not designed from scratch.\n\n**The artifact: a claim-anchored "Perspectives" panel** that opens from any contested sentence (reusing the compare-view host), containing per legitimate perspective:\n\n1. **A neutral position header** — "Position held by [who], with this evidence behind it" — no "fringe"/"warning"/"debunked". A steelmanned one-line statement of the view in neutral terms.\n2. **An evidence-basis sub-panel (GRADE-style, the load-bearing element):** the study types / source tiers / independent-origin count behind that perspective, rendered as …121698 tokens truncated…md:1397:    codex_audit_verdict: APPROVE_PENDING

.\docs\credibility_adaptive_weighting_and_bothsides_recs_2026_06_08.md:1:# POLARIS Source-Credibility & Multi-Perspective Recommendations Report\n### Driving two revisions to `docs/credibility_weighted_sourcing_redesign_plan_2026_06_07.md` — LAYER 1 (scoring) and LAYER 6 (composition + UI)\n\n**Author:** Lead analyst (Claude). **Date:** 2026-06-08.\n**Inputs:** three research streams (per-question adaptive credibility weighting; neutral multi-perspective presentation; friendly UI/artifact patterns).\n**Status:** revision driver. Each layer below states what it **REPLACES** in the Codex-APPROVE'd 2026-06-07 plan, then the concrete mechanism, auditability, reliability, and POLARIS wiring.\n\n**Invariants preserved across both revisions** (these are not negotiable and the revisions do not weaken them): the LLM credibility-judge is **advisory only** — `strict_verify`'s six per-sentence checks (`provenance_generator.py:1156`) remain the binding faithfulness gate; every new layer is **flag-gated, default-OFF byte-identical**, fail-loud on missing inputs; weight is **evidence quality/tier, never headcount**; every displayed aggregate is **one click from the cited `[#ev:id:start-end]` span and its VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict**; the credibility prior stays **self-computed and verifier-overridable** (no single external rater hardwired); independence-collapse (`synthesis/independence_collapse.py`) still runs before any weighted tally; the contested-topic adjudication **reuses the existing 4-role / voter-arbiter pipeline** (`roles/role_pipeline.py` + `honest_sweep_integration.py`), open-weight voters only — no parallel path is built.\n\n---\n\n## 1. LAYER 1 (scoring): adaptive per-question credibility-skill, replacing the fixed domain-rubric selector\n\n### 1.1 What this REPLACES\n\nThe 2026-06-07 plan's **Phase 2a/2b (L1)** selects one of **three fixed reliability rubrics** (clinical → RCT+peer-review+RoB; econ/policy → design-validity; qualitative → CERQual) keyed off the detected domain. That is still a small lookup table: domain → rubric. The operator constraint is explicit — **replace fixed domain rubrics** with a **generic, domain-agnostic credibility skill the LLM applies by reasoning per question**. Research stream #1's central finding is that the frontier (OpenAI, Gemini, Claude) has already moved this way, and that Perplexity's baked-in EEAT/domain-authority scoring is the closest-to-forbidden counter-example (gameable, popularity-biased, ~60% Google-overlap). We copy the reasoned-generic camp.\n\nThe revision: **domain stops being a selector and becomes context that primes one generic skill.** There is exactly one credibility skill; the detected `scope_template` domain is passed in as a hint the skill reasons over ("this is a clinical efficacy question, so weight trial design and RoB heavily"), not a branch that swaps rubrics. This scales to 10,000+ fields with zero per-field config.\n\n### 1.2 The exact mechanism — credibility-skill / guardrail prompt × (reliability × relevance)\n\n**Step A — deterministic signals (POLARIS produces these; unchanged substrate).** `authority_model.score_source_authority` and `tier_classifier` already emit, per source, the field-agnostic primitives: `authority_score [0,1]`, `source_class`, `corroboration_count` (independent-host agreement), `authority_confidence`, `signal_scores` (the A–E sub-scores), plus `junk_class` / `predatory_oa` (`source_class.py:71-89`). Independence-collapse (`independence_collapse.py`) emits `origin_cluster_id` + canonical-origin designation + copy flag. **None of this is replaced.** These are the inspectable, host-name-free, self-computed inputs (LAW VI: zero host literals in code).\n\n**Step B — the credibility skill consumes those signals and weights them per question.** A new pure prompt module, `authority/credibility_skill.py`, runs a **JudgeRank-style 3-step decomposition** (arXiv 2411.00142) — chosen because each step is inspectable text and is itself the audit template:\n\n1. **Query analysis** — identify what THIS question actually needs (the claim type, what would count as strong evidence for it).\n2. **Source analysis** — for each candidate source, a query-AWARE assessment applying **generic SIFT + lateral-reading + provenance heuristics**, NOT a domain table. The skill's instruction block encodes the domain-agnostic primacy heuristics that are OpenAI's own deep-research pattern: *prefer the primary/official source over an aggregator or SEO blog; prefer the original paper over a survey/secondary summary; corroborate laterally (does independent coverage agree); weigh source incentives/track record; downgrade stale-but-authoritative and retracted/superseded* (the latter wires to the existing `supersession.py` Phase 3 signal).\n3. **Two-axis judgment with rationale** — emit, per source, **RELIABILITY × RELEVANCE** (the EFSA/OHAT weight-of-evidence two-axis, which POLARIS currently conflates into one tier): reliability = internal validity/method given what the skill read in the signals; relevance = directness to this specific question. The product is the per-question credibility weight. **Crucially, the skill is told its priors are the `authority_model` signals and that it may up- or down-weight them with a stated reason** — it does not invent authority from nothing, and it cannot silently override `authority_confidence=LOW` into a fabricated HIGH (thin OpenAlex/ROR signal stays honestly LOW).\n\n**Output schema (machine-parseable, bound to the schema discipline already in §8.3.9):** per source — `{reliability_score, relevance_score, credibility_weight, rationale_string, signals_cited:[...]}`. The weight is **a visible, revisable rationale string, never a hidden scalar and never a fine-tuned-in behavior** (this is why we reject the CAG fine-tune approach from stream #1: opaque learned weights are exactly the auditability failure POLARIS differentiates against — borrow CAG's *evidence* that credibility-conditioning gives noise robustness, and its three generic dimensions of relevance/timeliness/reliability, but implement them at inference time as a prompt-visible signal).\n\n### 1.3 How it stays AUDITABLE (auditable by construction, not bolted on)\n\nThe judgment IS a reasoning trace, so it is emitted verbatim and **bound to the same provenance substrate POLARIS already has**:\n\n- The per-source `credibility_weight` + `rationale_string` + `signals_cited` attach to the source's `AuthorityResult` as **additive fields** (mirroring how `signal_scores`, `junk_class`, `predatory_oa` are already additive side-outputs on the dataclass), emitted on rows in `tier_classifier.py`.\n- At claim time, the weight flows into the four Phase-1/Phase-8 disclosure fields on `SentenceVerification` (`credibility_weight`, `independent_origin_count`, `certainty_label`, `span_verdict`), so each verified sentence shows **which source was weighted how, and why**, one click from its `[#ev]` span.\n- Because the skill cites the deterministic `signals_cited` it reasoned from, the rationale is **checkable against the inputs** — a reviewer can confirm "preferred A over B because A is the primary trial-registry entry and B a secondary news summary" against the actual `source_class` values. The rationale is a **claim to verify, not ground truth** (post-hoc rationalization risk per stream #1) — so it is advisory and the binding gate stays `strict_verify`.\n\nThis is the §-1.1-compliant story: no metadata/count/string-presence signal, every weight traceable to a cited span and an inspectable reason.\n\n### 1.4 Reliability and where it fails (and the guardrail)\n\nStream #1 is blunt about the failure modes, and they bound the design: LLMs "treat all retrieved documents as equally valid" unless explicitly steered and over-rely on high-frequency claims (arXiv 2505.17762); AuthorityBench (2603.25092) shows authority perception is **inconsistent across domains and highly prompt-sensitive**, struggles with false authority, and exhibits position/verbosity/self-preference bias. Therefore:\n\n- **The skill is ADVISORY to ranking/selection, never the faithfulness gate.** It changes *which rows are billed/weighted*, not *whether a sentence verifies its span*. `strict_verify`, 4-role/two-family segregation, and the independent `corpus_approval_gate` tier-distribution backstop all still run sequentially.\n- **Bias mitigations baked into the prompt:** score rationale-first then number; randomize candidate order to blunt position bias; run pointwise (per-source) to avoid listwise permutation instability.\n- **Offline validation before trust:** the chosen judge model+prompt is validated on an **AuthorityBench-style harness** (authority-PERCEPTION only, per the §6a no-overstatement correction — not as a volume-vulnerability benchmark) plus the existing vax adversarial fixture, before it is allowed on the shipping path. Calibration (Brier/ECE) on the emitted weights runs in the existing Phase 11 harness.\n- **Capture resistance:** multi-signal, self-computed, verifier-overridable — no NewsGuard/MBFC/Ad Fontes verdict is hardwired as ground truth (the FTC-capture risk).\n\n### 1.5 The honest gap + exactly what POLARIS builds for L1\n\n**HAVE:** deterministic authority signals (`authority_model`, `tier_classifier`), the additive `AuthorityResult`/`SentenceVerification` schema, independence-collapse, `scope_templates` domain detection, the JSON-verdict schema discipline.\n**MISSING:** the generic per-question credibility skill itself, and the second (relevance) axis.\n**BUILD (revision to Phase 2a/2b):**\n1. `authority/credibility_skill.py` — the pure 3-step (query→source→two-axis-judgment) prompt module emitting `{reliability, relevance, credibility_weight, rationale, signals_cited}`. Domain is an input *hint*, not a rubric switch. (Replaces the fixed-rubric selector in `credibility_prior.py`.)\n2. Add `relevance_score` (and the rationale fields) to `AuthorityResult` (`source_class.py:75`); emit on rows in `tier_classifier.py`.\n3. Wire the skill's weight into the L5 weight-mass tally and the L7 disclosure fields — advisory input, not a gate.\n4. Flag-gated default-OFF byte-identical; OFF = the legacy single-scalar path, byte-for-byte.\n\n---\n\n## 2. LAYER 6 (composition + UI): neutral multi-perspective + transparent evidence-weight artifact, replacing the forewarning/fringe framing\n\n### 2.1 What this REPLACES\n\nThe 2026-06-07 plan's **Phase 7 (L6)** composes contested claims as "consensus at high weight + minority attributed at low weight **with explicit forewarning**, medical-misinfo **low-weight/fringe**, ABSTAIN over fabricated balance." The operator directive is to **replace the forewarning/fringe framing** with a **neutral multi-perspective presentation where competing world-views are shown as legitimate, each carrying its real (possibly asymmetric) evidence weight, and the user judges** — no bias, no stamps, no forewarning prose.\n\n### 2.2 The hard tension, named and resolved (do not skip this)\n\nThere is a real conflict between two binding constraints, and both sides have a lethal failure mode:\n\n- The operator wants **no fringe/forewarning stamp, all sides legitimate, no bias.**\n- The **clinical-safety invariant #5** (binding, preserved) plus Dixon-Clarke 2013 (PubMed 23193194, measured harm: falsely-balanced vaccine reporting *reduced* perceived safety and vaccination intent), Wikipedia FRINGE, and §-1.1 all say **equal treatment of unequal evidence is itself bias** and is "lethal in clinical." I am not authorized to drop invariant #5.\n\n**The reconciliation — handed to us nearly verbatim by all three streams: replace the LABEL with the BASIS.** Wikipedia NPOV's "neutral *editing*, not neutral *content*"; GRADE's "show the basis, let the user infer"; the no-warning rule from stream #2 is satisfiable **if and only if the criteria behind any weight are displayed**. So:\n\n- The **system** stamps nothing — no "fringe," no "debunked," no forewarning sentence. That is the neutrality.\n- The **evidence weight** carries the (often asymmetric) truth, rendered as a visible **per-perspective evidence-basis panel** the user reads and judges. The asymmetry — *14 RCTs + 3 systematic reviews [High]* vs *2 case reports + mechanistic argument [Very Low]* — becomes **visible in the artifact** instead of **asserted in a stamp**. The user infers; the system does not editorialize.\n- "Legitimate" means **shown with its real (possibly low) weight and one-click drill-down to span + verdict** — NOT "shown as equally supported." A genuine world-view dispute with no empirical consensus (values, forecasting) shows steelmanned sides at honest parity; an empirical dispute with consensus shows the real weight distribution.\n- The medical-misinfo case is handled **without the banned word**: its panel is simply **near-empty of independent high-tier basis**, and where there is no independent consensus the claim **ABSTAINs** ("contested; no independent consensus" — reusing existing refuse/unresolved behavior). This preserves invariant #5's *substance* (not normalized as an equal side) while dropping the stamp.\n\nThis is neutral AND anti-false-balance AND §-1.1-safe simultaneously — the operator's "let the user judge" satisfied by *showing the basis*, not by *equalizing the boxes*.\n\n### 2.3 The exact composition mechanism\n\nPer question, the composition path first **diagnoses the contestation type** (this IS the adaptive guardrail, copied from Anthropic's even-handedness "lack-of-consensus" discriminator + OpenAI's seek-the-truth-together):\n\n- **empirical-with-consensus** (vaccines, climate) → due-weight: each side shown, weight proportional to verified-evidence quality; the asymmetry is the message, carried by the basis panel.\n- **genuine-uncertainty** (open scientific questions) → separate *supported* from *open*; sides at honest parity.\n- **values dispute** (politics, ethics) → **steelman each legitimate view** (Ideological Turing Test, neutral terminology, no verdict); no evidence-weight asymmetry asserted because there is no due weight to defer to.\n- **forecasting** (AI-and-jobs) → scenario spread, projective not factual.\n\nEach perspective is gathered through its **own retrieval lens** (MODS-style per-perspective retrieval + citation, arXiv 2502.00322 — raw LLMs silently drop minority views; per-perspective retrieval prevents the drop), then composed via the **existing 4-role / voter-arbiter agreement** (cross-lineage, open-weight voters — the bridging/balanced-panel analog) — **not a new adjudication path**. Reranking-for-balance (arXiv 2506.15925) selects the most balanced faithful candidate, because direct just-prompt-balanced generation empirically skews. **The weight attached to each perspective is evidence QUALITY × independent-origin count, never document count** — else we rebuild Ground News's source-count bias inside the summarizer.\n\n### 2.4 The friendly UI artifact — design\n\nBuilt on the **components that already exist** (#744 citation chip + hover source card, #745 per-claim verdict chip, #747 Proof Replay split-view, #757 report page, #758 claim-anchored compare view) — not designed from scratch.\n\n**The artifact: a claim-anchored "Perspectives" panel** that opens from any contested sentence (reusing the compare-view host), containing per legitimate perspective:\n\n1. **A neutral position header** — "Position held by [who], with this evidence behind it" — no "fringe"/"warning"/"debunked". A steelmanned one-line statement of the view in neutral terms.\n2. **An evidence-basis sub-panel (GRADE-style, the load-bearing element):** the study types / source tiers / independent-origin count behind that perspective, rendered as **frequencies, not a percentage or a lone dot** — "*8 of n: RCTs + systematic reviews [High certainty]*" vs "*2 of n: case reports + mechanistic argument [Very Low]*". The certainty label is acceptable **only because its downgrade criteria are shown** (study design / consistency / directness / independence). This makes the asymmetry self-evident without a stamp.\n3. **Scite-style polarity badges** (supporting / contrasting / contextualizing) on each cited source — **neutral hue + icon + text label, never color alone** (colorblind safety; red=contrasting reads as red=wrong and biases toward consensus — explicitly avoided).\n4. **Drill-down:** every badge, every basis count, every panel is **one click from the raw `[#ev]` span and its VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict** — the Scite "self-correcting" property: a mis-classified badge is exposed by the citing sentence sitting right behind it, and a meter without drill-down would violate the §-1.1 metadata-audit ban.\n\n**Panel sizing defeats false balance structurally, not with a caveat:** panels are **sized/annotated by real verified-evidence weight**, not equal-width — because equal real estate reads as equal credibility (the false-balance trap), and a caveat is empirically insufficient (Effectiviology / false-balance literature). The asymmetry is *in the layout and the basis panel*, not asserted in prose.\n\n**Three named anti-patterns explicitly rejected** (all from the streams, all as negative templates):\n- **Ground News source-count / coverage bar** — measures who-is-saying-this (volume), not evidence weight; §-1.1 bans source counts as quality signals. If a composition strip is shown at all, its axis is **evidence tier / source type**, never ideology or headcount, and it is kept visually separate from the weight panel so "many sources" never reads as "true."\n- **Bare confidence/credibility score (% or traffic-light dot)** — the best-documented HARM pattern: overconfident displays (80% shown / 70% accurate) pushed AI-advice adoption 57%→69.6%, 64% of users mis-judged calibration, and in a 2025 breast-cancer CDSS high confidence *reduced* diagnostic accuracy via overreliance. POLARIS's honest replacement is the per-sentence VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict against a real span — never a glanceable dot.\n- **Symmetric 50/50 equal-box presentation** — manufactures false balance; the Dixon-Clarke measured harm.\n\n### 2.5 The honest gap + exactly what POLARIS builds for L6\n\n**HAVE:** the disclosure substrate (per-sentence `[#ev]` tokens, `strict_verify` verdict ladder, `SentenceVerification` additive fields), the existing 4-role/voter-arbiter agreement, independence-collapse for origin-count, and the full UI component kit (citation chip, verdict chip, Proof Replay, compare view).\n**MISSING:** the contestation-type classifier, per-perspective retrieval + composition that defeats false balance by weight, and the Perspectives artifact rendering basis panels.\n**BUILD (revision to Phase 7):**\n1. A **contestation-type classifier** (empirical-consensus / genuine-uncertainty / values / forecasting) priming the composition rule — replaces the fixed forewarning+fringe rule.\n2. **Per-perspective retrieval + balance-rerank composition** over the post-collapse origins, weighting each perspective by verified-evidence quality × independent-origin count (not count).\n3. A **steelman + GRADE-style evidence-basis renderer** feeding a new **claim-anchored "Perspectives" panel** in the compare-view host: neutral headers, frequency-framed basis sub-panels, Scite-style neutral polarity badges, full span-verdict drill-down, weight-proportional sizing.\n4. Validated with a **paired-prompt neutrality eval** (Anthropic's open-sourced political-neutrality harness, adapted so it does NOT reward equal treatment of unequal evidence) + the vax adversarial fixture (asserts the asymmetry renders, no stamp, no 50/50).\n5. Flag-gated default-OFF byte-identical; ABSTAIN reuses existing refuse/unresolved behavior; forewarning prose removed, replaced by the basis panel.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Consolidated "build" summary\n\n| Layer | Replaces (2026-06-07 plan) | POLARIS builds | Binding gate untouched |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| **L1 scoring** | Fixed 3-rubric domain selector (Phase 2a/2b) | `credibility_skill.py` — generic 3-step SIFT/lateral-reading skill, reliability×relevance, rationale bound to `AuthorityResult`/`[#ev]`; domain as hint not switch; `relevance_score` axis | `strict_verify` binding; skill advisory; corpus_approval backstop |\n| **L6 composition+UI** | Forewarning + fringe framing (Phase 7) | Contestation-type classifier + per-perspective retrieval/balance-rerank weighted by quality×origin-count + steelman/GRADE-basis "Perspectives" panel (replace label with basis) | 4-role/voter-arbiter reused (no parallel path); ABSTAIN reuses refuse/unresolved; invariant #5 substance preserved |\n\nHonest residual: L1's skill is prompt-sensitive and must clear offline AuthorityBench-style + calibration validation before it is trusted on the shipping path; L6's steelman is the hardest element to audit mechanically (no test certifies an argument is the strongest version vs a disguised strawman — the paired-prompt eval is the best available check, itself a judgment). Both remain advisory; `strict_verify` carries faithfulness.\n\n---\n\n## 4. .\outputs\audits\beatboth5\gemini_sanitized\Q75_metal_ions_cvd.md:111:Presented to the global medical community at the American College of Cardiology sessions in 2024, the results of the massive, double-blind, multicenter TACT2 trial delivered a final, totally definitive verdict: intravenous chelation therapy utilizing broad-spectrum EDTA is entirely, unequivocally ineffective as a modern cardiovascular therapy.48 The TACT2 trial randomized 959 high-risk patients (median age 67\) across 88 sites in the US and Canada to receive either 40 weekly intravenous infusions of 3 grams of EDTA or a saline placebo over a grueling 40-week period.48 Over a prolonged median clinical follow-up of 48 months, there was absolutely no statistically significant difference whatsoever between the aggressive EDTA group and the inert placebo group in the primary composite clinical endpoint of all-cause death, myocardial infarction, stroke, coronary revascularization, or hospitalization for unstable angina. The event rates were virtually identical: 35.6% for EDTA versus 35.7% for placebo, yielding a hazard ratio of 0.93 with a completely non-significant p-value of 0.53.48 Furthermore, secondary endpoints, including hard cardiovascular death, also showed absolutely no benefit.48

36: def _safe_log_str(text: str, max_len: int = 200) -> str:
37:     """Sanitize text for Windows console logging (cp1252 safe).
38: 
39:     Unicode chars like arrows, Greek letters, and math symbols cause
40:     UnicodeEncodeError on Windows cp1252 console handler. This replaces
41:     non-encodable chars with '?' before logging.
42:     """
43:     truncated = text[:max_len]
44:     try:
45:         truncated.encode("cp1252")
46:         return truncated
47:     except (UnicodeEncodeError, UnicodeDecodeError):
48:         return truncated.encode("ascii", errors="replace").decode("ascii")

53: # Explicitly request only gzip/deflate across ALL aiohttp sessions.
54: _NO_BROTLI_HEADERS = {"Accept-Encoding": "gzip, deflate"}

75: # FIX-EPIPE: Crawl4AI circuit breaker for subprocess crashes.
76: # After consecutive subprocess crashes (EPIPE, BrokenPipeError, OSError),
77: # skip crawl4ai entirely for a cooldown period to avoid cascading failures
78: # from a broken Playwright installation or dead browser process.

92: # I-fetch-002 (#1168): crawl4ai launches a Playwright browser subprocess PER URL; under the ~1000-URL
93: # benchmark fan-out, many concurrent browsers exhaust the OS and crash (EPIPE), which then trips the
94: # circuit breaker and disables crawl4ai run-wide. Bound the number of concurrently-LIVE browsers with a
95: # semaphore (mirrors the PG_JINA_CONCURRENCY=2 pattern). Lazy-init so it binds to the running loop.
96: _crawl4ai_semaphore: "asyncio.Semaphore | None" = None

99: def _get_crawl4ai_semaphore() -> "asyncio.Semaphore":
100:     """I-fetch-002 (#1168): lazy-init the crawl4ai browser-concurrency gate on the running loop.
101:     Default 2 concurrent browsers (env PG_CRAWL4AI_CONCURRENCY)."""
102:     global _crawl4ai_semaphore
103:     if _crawl4ai_semaphore is None:
104:         _crawl4ai_semaphore = asyncio.Semaphore(
105:             int(os.getenv("PG_CRAWL4AI_CONCURRENCY", "2"))
106:         )
107:     return _crawl4ai_semaphore

109: 
110: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
111: # BB5-S02 (#1177): cross-THREAD in-flight bypass-worker bound + leak gauge.
112: #
113: # `live_retriever._fetch_content` runs each `AccessBypass.fetch_with_bypass`
114: # on a fresh daemon thread with its OWN `asyncio.run` loop, joined with a hard
115: # timeout. On timeout the thread is ABANDONED (it keeps running, holding a live
116: # Crawl4AI/Playwright browser subprocess mid-`arun`). Under the ~740-URL
117: # benchmark fan-out, hundreds of abandoned threads + browser subprocesses
118: # accumulate (the resource-exhaustion / segfault mechanism).
119: #
120: # `_get_crawl4ai_semaphore()` cannot bound this: it is lazy-bound to the
121: # RUNNING loop, and every bypass worker thread has its OWN fresh loop — so it
122: # only caps browsers WITHIN one thread. A `threading`-level BoundedSemaphore is
123: # the only primitive that bounds the abandoned-thread FLEET across loops.
124: #
125: # Acquire at the TOP of the worker (in `live_retriever`), release in THAT
126: # worker's `finally` — never in the outer join path (releasing on abandonment
127: # would over-release; not releasing would leak the slot). Sized BELOW the
128: # parallel `max_workers` so it creates back-pressure; no deadlock because the
129: # inner per-backend wall-clocks guarantee every abandoned worker eventually
130: # terminates and releases its slot.
131: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
132: 
133: # Default ceiling on concurrently-LIVE bypass worker threads (each may hold a
134: # browser subprocess). Env-overridable. Below the live_retriever parallel
135: # `max_workers` ceiling (48) so abandoned in-flight workers cannot fan out a
136: # browser-per-candidate. Named constant (LAW VI — no magic numbers).
137: _BYPASS_INFLIGHT_DEFAULT_LIMIT = 16
138: PG_BYPASS_MAX_INFLIGHT_ENV = "PG_BYPASS_MAX_INFLIGHT"
139: 
140: _bypass_inflight_semaphore: "threading.BoundedSemaphore | None" = None
141: _bypass_inflight_semaphore_lock = threading.Lock()
142: 
143: # BB5-S02 leaked-worker gauge: monotonically-incremented count of bypass worker
144: # threads that were ABANDONED (outer join timed out while the worker was still
145: # alive). A non-zero gauge is the auditable signal that orphan browser
146: # subprocesses may have accumulated. Guarded by its own lock.
147: _bypass_leaked_worker_count: int = 0
148: _bypass_leaked_worker_lock = threading.Lock()
149: 
150: 
151: def _get_bypass_inflight_semaphore() -> "threading.BoundedSemaphore":
152:     """BB5-S02 (#1177): lazy-init the cross-thread in-flight bypass-worker
153:     bound. A `threading.BoundedSemaphore` (NOT asyncio) — it must bound worker
154:     threads across their independent per-thread event loops.
155: 
156:     Limit from `PG_BYPASS_MAX_INFLIGHT` (positive int), else
157:     `_BYPASS_INFLIGHT_DEFAULT_LIMIT`. A malformed/<=0 value falls back to the
158:     default — a bad knob must never disable the bound (which would re-open the
159:     abandoned-fleet leak)."""
160:     global _bypass_inflight_semaphore
161:     if _bypass_inflight_semaphore is None:
162:         with _bypass_inflight_semaphore_lock:
163:             if _bypass_inflight_semaphore is None:
164:                 raw = os.getenv(PG_BYPASS_MAX_INFLIGHT_ENV)
165:                 limit = _BYPASS_INFLIGHT_DEFAULT_LIMIT
166:                 if raw is not None and raw.strip():
167:                     try:
168:                         parsed = int(raw)
169:                         if parsed > 0:
170:                             limit = parsed
171:                     except ValueError:
172:                         limit = _BYPASS_INFLIGHT_DEFAULT_LIMIT
173:                 _bypass_inflight_semaphore = threading.BoundedSemaphore(limit)
174:     return _bypass_inflight_semaphore
175: 
176: 
177: def record_bypass_leaked_worker() -> int:
178:     """BB5-S02 (#1177): increment + return the leaked-bypass-worker gauge. The
179:     caller (live_retriever) invokes this when an outer fetch join times out
180:     while the worker thread is still alive (abandoned → potential orphan
181:     browser subprocess). Thread-safe; returns the new total for logging."""
182:     global _bypass_leaked_worker_count
183:     with _bypass_leaked_worker_lock:
184:         _bypass_leaked_worker_count += 1
185:         return _bypass_leaked_worker_count
186: 
187: 
188: def bypass_leaked_worker_count() -> int:
189:     """BB5-S02 (#1177): read the current leaked-bypass-worker gauge (auditable
190:     orphan-subprocess signal). Thread-safe snapshot."""
191:     with _bypass_leaked_worker_lock:
192:         return _bypass_leaked_worker_count

195: def reset_bypass_leak_state() -> None:
196:     """BB5-S02 (#1177): reset the leak gauge + in-flight semaphore. For test
197:     isolation ONLY — not called on the production path."""
198:     global _bypass_leaked_worker_count, _bypass_inflight_semaphore
199:     with _bypass_leaked_worker_lock:
200:         _bypass_leaked_worker_count = 0
201:     with _bypass_inflight_semaphore_lock:

205: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
206: # BB5-S03 (#1177): SIGSEGV-mitigated shared trafilatura extractor.
207: #
208: # `trafilatura.extract` runs libxml2 (a C extension). On a pathological /
209: # malformed / adversarial document libxml2 can SIGSEGV (drb_76 exit 139) — a
210: # C-level crash that is NOT a Python exception and CANNOT be caught by
211: # `except Exception`. A try/except around the call is false confidence.
212: #
213: # True containment is a per-page hard-killable subprocess, but that is heavy at
214: # hundreds of calls/run AND `resource` RLIMIT is Unix-only (no-op on win32).
215: # So the DEFAULT is lean MITIGATION (not containment): size-bound the HTML and
216: # prefer the caller's regex fallback for oversized/suspect docs, which never
217: # enters libxml2 at all. An optional hard-killable subprocess path is gated
218: # behind `PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS=1` (OFF by default).
219: #
220: # Lives in access_bypass (NOT live_retriever): live_retriever already imports
221: # access_bypass, so the reverse import would be circular. Both trafilatura
222: # sites import this one guarded entrypoint.
223: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
224: 
225: # Upper bound (chars) on HTML handed to libxml2 via trafilatura. A document
226: # larger than this is treated as suspect/oversized: we skip trafilatura and
227: # signal the caller to use its regex fallback (which never enters the C
228: # extension). Env-overridable. Named constant (LAW VI).
229: _TRAFILATURA_MAX_HTML_CHARS = int(
230:     os.getenv("PG_TRAFILATURA_MAX_HTML_CHARS", "3000000")
231: )
232: PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS_ENV = "PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS"
233: # Hard wall-clock for the optional subprocess extractor path (seconds).
234: _TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS_TIMEOUT = float(
235:     os.getenv("PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS_TIMEOUT_SECONDS", "20")
236: )
237: 
238: 
239: def _html_is_extract_safe(html: str) -> bool:
240:     """BB5-S03 (#1177): cheap pre-validation gate. Returns False for an
241:     oversized document (over `_TRAFILATURA_MAX_HTML_CHARS`) that should bypass
242:     libxml2 entirely. Pure size check — no parsing, never itself crashes."""
243:     if not html:
244:         return False
245:     if len(html) > _TRAFILATURA_MAX_HTML_CHARS:
246:         return False
247:     return True
248: 
249: 
250: def _trafilatura_extract_subprocess(html: str, **kwargs: Any) -> "str | None":
251:     """BB5-S03 (#1177): run `trafilatura.extract` in a hard-killable child
252:     process so a libxml2 SIGSEGV takes down the child (exit 139) instead of the
253:     sweep. Returns the extracted text, or None on timeout/crash/error.
254: 
255:     Gated OFF by default (`PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS=1` to enable) — true
256:     containment is heavy at hundreds of calls/run. Best-effort: any failure
257:     (spawn error, non-zero exit incl. -11/139 SIGSEGV, timeout) returns None so
258:     the caller falls back to regex extraction. Never raises."""
259:     import json
260:     import subprocess
261: 
262:     payload = json.dumps({"html": html, "kwargs": kwargs})
263:     code = (
264:         "import sys, json\n"
265:         "data = json.loads(sys.stdin.read())\n"
266:         "import trafilatura\n"
267:         "out = trafilatura.extract(data['html'], **data['kwargs']) or ''\n"
268:         "sys.stdout.write(out)\n"
269:     )
270:     try:
271:         proc = subprocess.run(
272:             [sys.executable, "-c", code],
273:             input=payload,
274:             capture_output=True,
275:             text=True,
276:             timeout=_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS_TIMEOUT,
277:         )
278:     except (subprocess.TimeoutExpired, OSError, ValueError) as exc:
279:         logger.warning(
280:             "[ACCESS] BB5-S03 trafilatura subprocess failed (%s) — "
281:             "regex fallback", type(exc).__name__,
282:         )
283:         return None
284:     if proc.returncode != 0:
285:         # A negative return code is a signal (e.g. -11 == SIGSEGV / exit 139):
286:         # the child crashed on a pathological doc and the SWEEP survived.
287:         logger.warning(
288:             "[ACCESS] BB5-S03 trafilatura subprocess exited rc=%s "
289:             "(SIGSEGV-class crash contained) — regex fallback",
290:             proc.returncode,
291:         )
292:         return None
293:     return proc.stdout or None
294: 
295: 
296: def safe_trafilatura_extract(html: str, **kwargs: Any) -> "str | None":
297:     """BB5-S03 (#1177): the ONE guarded trafilatura entrypoint used by every
298:     extraction site (live_retriever `_strip_html`, access_bypass
299:     `_try_crawl4ai`).
300: 
301:     Contract:
302:       - Returns extracted text (str) on success, or None when extraction is
303:         unsafe/empty/failed (caller falls back to its own regex path).
304:       - Honest MITIGATION, not containment, on the default in-process path:
305:         an oversized/suspect doc skips libxml2 (returns None → regex fallback);
306:         a SIGSEGV on a doc that passes the size gate is still uncatchable
307:         in-process. Enable `PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS=1` for true containment.
308:       - Never raises (the C-extension SIGSEGV is the one thing it cannot
309:         promise to catch on the in-process path — documented, not hidden)."""
310:     if not _html_is_extract_safe(html):
311:         return None
312:     if os.getenv(PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS_ENV, "0") == "1":
313:         return _trafilatura_extract_subprocess(html, **kwargs)
314:     try:
315:         import trafilatura  # type: ignore
316:         return trafilatura.extract(html, **kwargs) or None
317:     except Exception as exc:  # noqa: BLE001 — Python-level errors only; a
318:         # libxml2 SIGSEGV is NOT a Python exception and escapes this guard (by
319:         # design — that is what PG_TRAFILATURA_SUBPROCESS=1 contains).
320:         logger.debug(
321:             "[ACCESS] BB5-S03 trafilatura in-process extract error (%s) — "
322:             "regex fallback", type(exc).__name__,
323:         )
324:         return None

 succeeded in 7313ms:

242: 
243: # Conservative default — any backend not explicitly configured
244: # in `per_backend_max_concurrent` gets this limit. Operators
245: # can tune for known backends (Semantic Scholar = 1 per their
246: # docs; Serper = 10; etc.) by passing a dict.
