249: 
250: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
251: # Harvest-loop poll interval (I-fetch-003 / BB5-C01)
252: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
253: 
254: 
255: # Upper bound on a single harvest-loop wait. The deadline is anchored at
256: # each task's OBSERVED start (`task_started_monotonic_by_index`), not submit,
257: # so a task that has not started yet can never be marked TIMEOUT. To detect
258: # a task that STARTS after the previous snapshot (or one that hangs) within
259: # a bounded delay of its own start-anchored budget, the harvest loop never
260: # waits unbounded: it re-snapshots start-times + recomputes the expired set
261: # at least this often. Small enough to be responsive, large enough to avoid
262: # a busy-poll. The actual wait is `min(next_deadline - now, this)`.
263: _HARVEST_POLL_INTERVAL_SECONDS = 2.0
264: 
265: 
266: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
267: # Global batch-budget termination guarantee (I-fetch-003 / BB5-C01 P1)
268: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
269: 
270: 
271: # The per-task START-anchored timeout guarantees a STARTED task terminates,
272: # but a never-started task carries a +inf deadline: if every worker thread is
273: # wedged on an abandoned (timed-out but un-cancellable) in-flight fetch, the
274: # queued siblings keep their +inf deadline and the harvest loop could spin
275: # forever. The GLOBAL batch budget is the backstop that guarantees
276: # `parallel_fetch` ALWAYS returns in bounded time even under all-workers-wedged
277: # + queued-siblings. When the budget fires, every still-remaining future is
278: # recorded — started-but-unfinished as TIMEOUT (it ran, over-ran its budget),
279: # never-started as NOT_DISPATCHED (it never reached the fetcher) — and the
280: # harvest loop breaks.
281: #
282: # Operators override the budget directly with this env var (seconds). When
283: # UNSET, the budget is DERIVED from `per_task_timeout` and the number of
284: # submission waves: `per_task_timeout * (ceil(len(deduped)/max_workers)
285: # + _BATCH_BUDGET_WAVE_SLACK)`. `ceil(len/max_workers)` is the number of waves
286: # needed to run every task once if each task takes a full per_task_timeout; the
287: # slack adds head-room so a healthy batch (tasks finishing well inside budget,
288: # semaphore queuing) is never tripped spuriously.
289: PG_PARALLEL_FETCH_BATCH_BUDGET_SECONDS_ENV = (
290:     "PG_PARALLEL_FETCH_BATCH_BUDGET_SECONDS"
291: )
292: _BATCH_BUDGET_WAVE_SLACK = 2
293: 
294: 
295: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
296: # Round-robin submit ordering (I-fetch-003 / BB5-C02)
297: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
298: 
299: 
300: def _round_robin_indices(
301:     tasks: Sequence[FetchTask],
302: ) -> list[int]:
303:     """Return ORIGINAL task indices reordered into round-robin
304:     `backend_id` order.
305: 
306:     Group indices by `backend_id` (preserving first-seen group order
307:     and intra-group input order), then emit one index per backend per
308:     round until every group is exhausted. So the first ``len(groups)``
309:     indices span distinct backends/hosts.
310: 
311:     The result is a permutation of ``range(len(tasks))`` — every input
312:     index appears exactly once — so callers map results back to the
313:     ORIGINAL index unchanged. Pure / deterministic / allocation-light.
314:     """
315:     groups: dict[str, list[int]] = {}
316:     for idx, task in enumerate(tasks):
317:         groups.setdefault(task.backend_id, []).append(idx)
318: 
319:     ordered: list[int] = []
320:     group_queues = list(groups.values())
321:     while group_queues:
322:         next_round: list[list[int]] = []
323:         for queue in group_queues:
324:             ordered.append(queue.pop(0))
325:             if queue:
326:                 next_round.append(queue)
327:         group_queues = next_round
328:     return ordered
329: 
330: 
331: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
332: # Global batch-budget derivation (I-fetch-003 / BB5-C01 P1)
333: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
334: 
335: 
336: def _derive_batch_budget_seconds(
337:     *,
338:     num_tasks: int,
339:     max_workers: int,
340:     per_task_timeout: float | None,

 succeeded in 9420ms:
599: ### 8.3.9 Output schema bound (every brief specifies)
600: 
601: ```yaml
602: verdict: APPROVE | REQUEST_CHANGES
603: novel_p0: [...]
604: continuing_p0: [...]
605: p1: [...]
606: p2: [...]

 succeeded in 11743ms:
520:                     payload=None,
521:                     content_type=None,
522:                     fetch_status_code=None,
523:                     error=str(exc),
524:                     started_at=task_started,
525:                     finished_at=time.time(),
526:                     task_metadata=task.task_metadata,
527:                 )
528: 
529:             if (
530:                 not isinstance(result, tuple)
531:                 or len(result) != 3
532:                 or not isinstance(result[0], (bytes, bytearray))
533:                 or not isinstance(result[1], str)
534:                 or not isinstance(result[2], int)
535:             ):
536:                 raise FetcherProtocolError(
537:                     f"fetcher.fetch({task.source_url!r}) returned "
538:                     f"{type(result).__name__}, expected "
539:                     "tuple[bytes, str, int]"
540:                 )
541: 
542:             payload, content_type, status = result
543:             return FetchResultRecord(
544:                 source_url=task.source_url,
545:                 backend_id=task.backend_id,
546:                 outcome=FetchOutcome.SUCCESS,
547:                 payload=bytes(payload),
548:                 content_type=content_type,
549:                 fetch_status_code=status,
550:                 error=None,
551:                 started_at=task_started,
552:                 finished_at=time.time(),
553:                 task_metadata=task.task_metadata,
554:             )
555:         finally:
556:             sem.release()
557: 
558:     results_by_index: dict[int, FetchResultRecord] = {}
559: 
560:     # Codex round-1 HIGH fix (v2): manage executor manually so we
561:     # can shutdown(wait=False, cancel_futures=True) on TIMEOUT.
562:     # The `with` block's __exit__ calls shutdown(wait=True) which
563:     # blocks until all in-flight workers finish — defeating
564:     # boundary 3's caller-latency promise.
565:     executor = concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor(
566:         max_workers=max_workers,
567:     )
568:     try:
569:         future_to_index: dict[concurrent.futures.Future, int] = {}
570:         # I-fetch-003 (BB5-C02): submit in ROUND-ROBIN backend order so the
571:         # first `max_workers` submissions span up to `max_workers` distinct
572:         # backends/hosts. Without this, a clustered same-host candidate prefix
573:         # makes the first workers all block on ONE host-semaphore (acquired
574:         # inside `_run_task`), starving distinct-host tasks queued behind them.
575:         # `_round_robin_indices` returns ORIGINAL deduped indices, so result
576:         # indexing into `results_by_index` is unchanged (correctness preserved).
577:         submit_order = _round_robin_indices(deduped)
578:         # I-fetch-003 (BB5-C01 P1): anchor the GLOBAL batch budget at submit.
579:         batch_start = time.monotonic()
580:         for idx in submit_order:
581:             task = deduped[idx]
582:             fut = executor.submit(_run_task, idx, task)
583:             future_to_index[fut] = idx
584: 
585:         # I-fetch-003 (BB5-C01 P1): derive the GLOBAL batch budget — the
586:         # termination backstop that guarantees this call returns in bounded
587:         # time even when every worker is wedged on an abandoned in-flight fetch
588:         # and the queued siblings keep their +inf per-task deadline. Env wins;
589:         # else derive from per_task_timeout and the wave count; else (no
590:         # per-task timeout AND no env) the batch budget is disabled (None),
591:         # preserving the existing "None disables timeout" contract.
592:         batch_budget = _derive_batch_budget_seconds(
593:             num_tasks=len(deduped),
594:             max_workers=max_workers,
595:             per_task_timeout=per_task_timeout,
596:         )
597: 
598:         remaining: set[concurrent.futures.Future] = set(future_to_index)
599:         protocol_error_to_raise: FetcherProtocolError | None = None
600: 
601:         def _effective_deadline_monotonic(idx: int) -> float:
602:             # I-fetch-003 (BB5-C01): START-anchored, MONOTONIC effective
603:             # deadline. A not-yet-started index (absent from the start map)
604:             # → +inf: it CANNOT TIMEOUT before it runs. A started index →
605:             # its OWN observed start + per_task_timeout. Caller holds
606:             # `task_started_lock`.
607:             started = task_started_monotonic_by_index.get(idx)
608:             if started is None:
609:                 return float("inf")
610:             return started + per_task_timeout  # type: ignore[operator]
611: 
612:         batch_deadline = (
613:             batch_start + batch_budget if batch_budget is not None else None
614:         )
615: 
616:         while remaining and protocol_error_to_raise is None:
617:             if per_task_timeout is None and batch_deadline is None:
618:                 # No per-task timeout AND no batch budget — just wait for the
619:                 # next completion (the original "None disables timeout" path).
620:                 done, _ = concurrent.futures.wait(
621:                     remaining,
622:                     return_when=concurrent.futures.FIRST_COMPLETED,
623:                 )
624:             else:
625:                 # I-fetch-003 (BB5-C01): BOUNDED-POLL harvest. The wait is
626:                 # ALWAYS bounded by `_HARVEST_POLL_INTERVAL_SECONDS`, never
627:                 # `timeout=None`, so a task that STARTS after this snapshot
628:                 # (or one that hangs), AND the GLOBAL batch deadline, are
629:                 # re-checked within the poll interval — the harvest never
630:                 # relies on a sibling completing to make progress. When there
631:                 # is no per-task timeout (batch budget only), the per-task
632:                 # deadlines are all +inf so the poll interval alone bounds the
633:                 # wait until the batch deadline fires.
634:                 now_mono = time.monotonic()
635:                 if per_task_timeout is None:
636:                     next_deadline = float("inf")
637:                 else:
638:                     with task_started_lock:
639:                         next_deadline = min(
640:                             _effective_deadline_monotonic(future_to_index[f])
641:                             for f in remaining
642:                         )
643:                 if batch_deadline is not None:
644:                     next_deadline = min(next_deadline, batch_deadline)
645:                 wait_timeout = min(
646:                     max(0.0, next_deadline - now_mono),
647:                     _HARVEST_POLL_INTERVAL_SECONDS,
648:                 )
649:                 done, _ = concurrent.futures.wait(
650:                     remaining,

codex

1214:     async def _try_crawl4ai(self, url: str) -> AccessResult:
1215:         """
1216:         Crawl4AI: Free, local, Playwright-based web crawler that generates
1217:         LLM-ready markdown.  No API key or credits required.
1218: 
1219:         FIX-EPIPE: Hardened against Node.js subprocess EPIPE/broken pipe
1220:         errors that can kill the Python server process. The Playwright
1221:         browser subprocess can crash (EPIPE on websocket close), and the
1222:         error propagates through AsyncWebCrawler.__aenter__/__aexit__.
1223: 
1224:         Defense layers:
1225:         1. Circuit breaker -- skip crawl4ai after repeated subprocess crashes
1226:         2. Import error catch -- handles corrupted crawl4ai installations
1227:         3. Explicit __aenter__/__aexit__ -- no `async with` so __aexit__
1228:            failures are caught independently via _safe_close_crawler()

1230:         5. asyncio.CancelledError catch (BaseException in Python 3.9+)
1231:         6. BaseException safety net (re-raises KeyboardInterrupt/SystemExit)

1234:           - PG_CRAWL4AI_ENABLED (default "1")

1236:           - PG_CRAWL4AI_CIRCUIT_BREAKER_THRESHOLD (default "3")
1237:           - PG_CRAWL4AI_CIRCUIT_BREAKER_COOLDOWN (default "120.0")

1240:         and converted to failure results.

1243:         global _crawl4ai_consecutive_failures, _crawl4ai_circuit_open_until

1262:         # Lazy import with availability caching.
1263:         # FIX-EPIPE: Catch all exceptions during import, not just ImportError.

1285:                 "[polaris graph] CRAWL4AI: FIX-EPIPE import failed with "

1919:     /Jina/Firecrawl, paywall detection) but pipeline A wasn't wired
1920:     to it. This is the wiring.
1921: 
1922:     The AccessBypass call is async; live_retriever's fetch loop is
1923:     sync by historical choice. We run the async call in a fresh event
1924:     loop per URL. Full async refactor of run_live_retrieval (with
1925:     asyncio.gather for concurrency) is tracked as R-RETRIEVE-ASYNC in
1926:     docs/todo_list.md.

1928:     Env opt-out: set PG_DISABLE_ACCESS_BYPASS=1 to fall back to the
1929:     naive httpx path (useful when Playwright/Crawl4AI is unavailable).

1931:     I-meta-007c: ``doi_hint`` / ``pmid_hint`` are optional identifiers carried
1932:     from the candidate's S2 metadata. When AccessBypass returns stub/empty/
1933:     paywalled content AND a DOI is resolvable (hint or extracted from the URL),
1934:     the OPEN-ACCESS resolver (Unpaywall v2 -> AccessBypass; else PubMed EFetch
1935:     abstract) is tried BEFORE giving up. Gated by PG_ENABLE_LIVE_OA_RESOLVER
1936:     (default "1"); fail-OPEN (resolver errors never break retrieval).
1937:     """

1975:     # (so an abandoned worker holds its slot until it truly terminates) and
1976:     # released in the worker's OWN finally — never in the outer join path

1986:     def _bypass_worker() -> None:
1987:         # BB5-S02: acquire a cross-thread in-flight slot. Bounds the number of
1988:         # concurrently-LIVE bypass workers (each may hold a browser subprocess)
1989:         # across all per-thread event loops — `_get_crawl4ai_semaphore` cannot,
1990:         # being lazy-bound to THIS thread's fresh loop only.

1992:         try:

2002:         except Exception as exc:  # noqa: BLE001
2003:             result_holder["error"] = exc
2004:         finally:
2005:             _inflight_sem.release()

The current S02 patch records abandonment but does not terminate the abandoned thread or its event loop; it relies on eventual completion. I’m going one layer deeper into `_try_crawl4ai` and the runner to verify whether cleanup is robust when the outer timeout fires.

503: _NUMERIC_TOKEN_RE = re.compile(r"\d+\.\d+|\d+\s*%|\d{3,}|\bp\s*[<=>]\s*0\.\d+\b")

505: 
506: def _score_content_quality(content: str) -> float:
507:     """Score a fetched-content candidate on quality (0.0 .. ~1.5).
508: 
509:     Combines normalized length, structural-marker hits, and numeric
510:     density. Fully stripped stubs and paywall shells score low; full
511:     article bodies with numeric data score high. Used to pick the winner
512:     when multiple concurrent backends (Crawl4AI, Jina, Trafilatura)
513:     return successful results — replaces first-success-wins, which let
514:     Jina stubs beat Crawl4AI full-article fetches.
515: 
516:     This is NOT just length: a long paywall page with repeated
517:     "subscribe to read" blocks will have no structural markers and low
518:     numeric density, so it loses to a shorter true article body.
519:     """
520:     if not content:
521:         return 0.0
522: 
523:     length = len(content)
524:     # 30K chars normalizes to 1.0 — NEJM/Lancet full articles are ~40-70K
525:     length_norm = min(length / 30000.0, 1.0)
526: 
527:     lower = content.lower()
528:     marker_hits = sum(1 for m in _STRUCTURAL_MARKERS if m in lower)
529:     marker_score = min(marker_hits / 6.0, 1.0)
530: 
531:     numeric_count = len(_NUMERIC_TOKEN_RE.findall(content))
532:     # Numeric tokens per KB of text; cap at 1.0
533:     density = min(numeric_count / max(length / 1000.0, 1.0) / 5.0, 1.0)
534: 
535:     return 0.5 * length_norm + 0.3 * marker_score + 0.2 * density

555:     """FIX-EPIPE: Increment crawl4ai failure counter and open circuit breaker

557:     breaker logic in every except branch."""

566:             "after %d consecutive failures (cooldown %.0fs)",

572: async def _safe_close_crawler(crawler: Any, url: str) -> None:
573:     """FIX-EPIPE: Safely close a crawl4ai AsyncWebCrawler instance.
574: 
575:     When the Playwright browser subprocess dies (EPIPE on websocket close),
576:     calling __aexit__ on the crawler will attempt to close the dead socket
577:     and raise BrokenPipeError. This function catches ALL exceptions from
578:     __aexit__ to prevent the cleanup from killing the server.
579: 
580:     Args:
581:         crawler: The AsyncWebCrawler instance to close.
582:         url: The URL being fetched (for logging only).
583:     """
584:     if crawler is None:
585:         return
586:     try:
587:         await crawler.__aexit__(None, None, None)
588:     except (BrokenPipeError, ConnectionError, OSError) as exit_err:
589:         # PRIMARY CRASH VECTOR: Browser subprocess died, socket is broken.
590:         # This is expected and non-fatal -- the crawl result (if any) is
591:         # already captured.
592:         logger.warning(
593:             "[polaris graph] CRAWL4AI: FIX-EPIPE browser cleanup pipe "
594:             "error for %s (non-fatal, server protected): %s: %s",
595:             _safe_log_str(url, 60),
596:             type(exit_err).__name__,
597:             _safe_log_str(str(exit_err)),
598:         )
599:     except asyncio.CancelledError:
600:         # Task cancellation during cleanup -- non-fatal.
601:         logger.warning(
602:             "[polaris graph] CRAWL4AI: FIX-EPIPE browser cleanup "
603:             "cancelled for %s (non-fatal)",
604:             _safe_log_str(url, 60),
605:         )
606:     except Exception as exit_err:
607:         logger.warning(
608:             "[polaris graph] CRAWL4AI: FIX-EPIPE browser cleanup "
609:             "exception for %s (non-fatal): %s: %s",
610:             _safe_log_str(url, 60),
611:             type(exit_err).__name__,
612:             _safe_log_str(str(exit_err)),
613:         )
614:     except BaseException as exit_err:
615:         # Even GeneratorExit or exotic BaseException subclasses from
616:         # native Playwright extensions must not kill the server.
617:         if isinstance(exit_err, (KeyboardInterrupt, SystemExit)):
618:             logger.warning(
619:                 "[polaris graph] CRAWL4AI: FIX-EPIPE browser cleanup "
620:                 "interrupted for %s -- re-raising",
621:                 _safe_log_str(url, 60),
622:             )
623:             raise
624:         logger.warning(
625:             "[polaris graph] CRAWL4AI: FIX-EPIPE browser cleanup "
626:             "BaseException for %s (non-fatal, server protected): %s: %s",
627:             _safe_log_str(url, 60),
628:             type(exit_err).__name__,
629:             _safe_log_str(str(exit_err)),
630:         )
631: 
632: 
633: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
634: # I-bug-114 (#551): per-backend hard wall-clock bound for the concurrent fetch
635: # fan-out. A single backend wedged in a Playwright op must not freeze the whole
636: # `asyncio.gather`. `_bounded_backend` returns within PG_BACKEND_FETCH_TIMEOUT
637: # + PG_BACKEND_CLEANUP_GRACE regardless of backend state — it uses
638: # `asyncio.wait` (which returns after its timeout unconditionally) and never
639: # `asyncio.wait_for` (which would await the cancelled coroutine's cleanup).
640: # The post-artifacts asyncio.run-teardown residual is tracked in #552.
641: # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
642: 
643: # Strong refs to backend tasks abandoned after the cancel-grace window — kept
644: # so they are not GC-warned; the done-callback also retrieves any exception.
645: _DETACHED_BACKEND_TASKS: "set[asyncio.Task]" = set()
646: 
647: 
648: def _backend_fetch_timeout() -> float:
649:     """Per-backend in-flight wall-clock ceiling (seconds)."""
650:     try:
651:         return float(os.getenv("PG_BACKEND_FETCH_TIMEOUT", "60.0"))
652:     except ValueError:
653:         return 60.0
654: 
655: 
656: def _backend_cleanup_grace() -> float:
657:     """Bounded grace window for a cancelled backend's cleanup (seconds)."""
658:     try:
659:         return float(os.getenv("PG_BACKEND_CLEANUP_GRACE", "10.0"))
660:     except ValueError:
661:         return 10.0
662: 
663: 
664: def _drain_detached(task: "asyncio.Task") -> None:
665:     """Done-callback for a detached backend task: drop the strong ref and
666:     retrieve any exception so asyncio does not log 'exception never retrieved'.
667:     """
668:     _DETACHED_BACKEND_TASKS.discard(task)
669:     if not task.cancelled():
670:         try:
671:             task.exception()
672:         except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 — exception retrieval is best-effort
673:             pass
674: 
675: 
676: def _force_drop_detached_task(task: "asyncio.Task") -> None:
677:     """I-cd-032 (#632): forcibly remove a wedged detached task from the
678:     main asyncio loop's await-list at teardown.
679: 
680:     `asyncio.run`'s built-in shutdown calls `_cancel_all_tasks` which
681:     `await`s every still-pending task. If a detached backend ignores
682:     cancellation, that await is unbounded.
683: 
684:     Mitigation: close the task's underlying coroutine via
685:     `_coro.close()` — this raises GeneratorExit in the coroutine,
686:     cleanup runs synchronously, and the task is finalized as cancelled
687:     so `_cancel_all_tasks` does not have to await it.
688: 
689:     Best-effort: if `_coro` is not accessible OR `close()` itself blocks
690:     (it shouldn't — close just raises GeneratorExit into the frame), the
691:     fallback path drops the strong reference and lets asyncio teardown
692:     proceed with the standard cancellation + await behavior.
693: 
694:     Called by an `asyncio.run`-teardown hook installed at run start.
695:     """
696:     if task.done():
697:         return
698:     coro = getattr(task, "_coro", None)
699:     if coro is None:
700:         return
701:     try:
702:         # close() raises GeneratorExit into the coroutine's current
703:         # suspension point, which runs any finally/except blocks but
704:         # cannot await anything new (GeneratorExit suppresses yields).
705:         coro.close()
706:     except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001 — close() must never raise here
707:         pass
708:     _DETACHED_BACKEND_TASKS.discard(task)
709: 
710: 
711: def install_teardown_drain_hook(loop: "asyncio.AbstractEventLoop") -> None:
712:     """I-cd-032 (#632) DEPRECATED — hooking loop.close() runs too late:
713:     `asyncio.run` calls `_cancel_all_tasks` (which awaits every pending
714:     task) BEFORE `loop.close()`, so a wedged detached task hangs the
715:     cancel-all phase. Use `polaris_asyncio_run()` below instead. Kept
716:     as a thin shim that ALSO patches `_cancel_all_tasks` for callers
717:     that already use `asyncio.run` directly.
718:     """
719:     original_close = loop.close
720: 
721:     def _drain_then_close() -> None:
722:         for task in list(_DETACHED_BACKEND_TASKS):
723:             _force_drop_detached_task(task)
724:         original_close()
725: 
726:     loop.close = _drain_then_close  # type: ignore[method-assign]
727: 
728: 
729: def polaris_asyncio_run(coro: Any) -> Any:
730:     """I-cd-032 (#632): drop-in replacement for `asyncio.run` that
731:     drains wedged detached backend tasks BEFORE the loop's
732:     `_cancel_all_tasks` phase awaits them.
733: 
734:     Sequence:
735:       1. Create a new event loop.
736:       2. Run the main coroutine to completion (or exception).
737:       3. **Drain `_DETACHED_BACKEND_TASKS` by force-closing each.** This
738:          must happen BEFORE `_cancel_all_tasks` so the task is already
739:          finalized (cancelled) when the standard shutdown iterates it.
740:       4. Mirror `asyncio.run`'s standard shutdown: cancel all remaining
741:          tasks, run them until complete, run async generator shutdown,
742:          shutdown default executor, close the loop.
743: 
744:     Replaces `asyncio.run(...)` at pipeline-A entry (`run_one_query`)
745:     when the run includes any Playwright-bound fetch backend.
746:     """
747:     loop = asyncio.new_event_loop()
748:     try:
749:         asyncio.set_event_loop(loop)
750:         main_task = loop.create_task(coro)
751:         try:
752:             return loop.run_until_complete(main_task)
753:         finally:
754:             # I-cd-032: force-close wedged detached tasks BEFORE the
755:             # standard cancel-all-tasks step so it has nothing
756:             # un-cancellable to await.
757:             for task in list(_DETACHED_BACKEND_TASKS):
758:                 _force_drop_detached_task(task)
759:             # Mirror asyncio.run's shutdown phases.
760:             try:
761:                 _polaris_cancel_all_tasks(loop)
762:                 loop.run_until_complete(loop.shutdown_asyncgens())
763:                 if hasattr(loop, "shutdown_default_executor"):
764:                     loop.run_until_complete(loop.shutdown_default_executor())
765:             finally:
766:                 asyncio.set_event_loop(None)
767:                 loop.close()
768:     except BaseException:
769:         # Ensure the loop is closed on any exception path.
770:         if not loop.is_closed():
771:             loop.close()
772:         raise
773: 
774: 
775: def _polaris_cancel_all_tasks(loop: "asyncio.AbstractEventLoop") -> None:
776:     """Mirror of stdlib asyncio.runners._cancel_all_tasks but with a
777:     GENUINE hard wall-clock. Codex iter-2 P0 fix: stdlib
778:     `asyncio.wait_for(asyncio.gather(...), timeout=2)` does NOT bound
779:     because gather's child-task cancellation cleanup continues past
780:     the wait_for's own cancellation. Use `asyncio.wait(..., timeout)`
781:     instead — it returns `(done, pending)` sets unconditionally at
782:     the timeout AND does not propagate cancellation to children.
783: 
784:     After the 2s wall, every task still in `pending` is force-closed
785:     via `_force_drop_detached_task` so the subsequent loop.close()
786:     has nothing pending to await.
787:     """
788:     to_cancel = [t for t in asyncio.all_tasks(loop) if not t.done()]
789:     if not to_cancel:
790:         return
791:     for task in to_cancel:
792:         task.cancel()
793: 
794:     async def _wait_with_hard_wall():
795:         # asyncio.wait returns (done, pending) at timeout — does NOT
796:         # await child-task cleanup beyond the wall. Defense-in-depth
797:         # against untracked wedged tasks.
798:         done, pending = await asyncio.wait(to_cancel, timeout=2.0)
799:         return done, pending
800: 
801:     try:
802:         _done, pending = loop.run_until_complete(_wait_with_hard_wall())
803:     except BaseException:
804:         # Best-effort — if even our wait helper raises, just force-
805:         # drop every pending task.
806:         pending = [t for t in to_cancel if not t.done()]
807: 
808:     for task in pending:
809:         if not task.done():
810:             _force_drop_detached_task(task)
811:

1606:     async def _extract_pdf_text(self, url: str) -> str:
1607:         """FIX-CITE-3/GAP4: Download and extract text from academic PDF.
1608: 
1609:         Uses PyMuPDF (fitz) for extraction. Falls back to basic text
1610:         extraction if PyMuPDF is not available.

1613:         import tempfile

824: 
825: async def _bounded_backend(label: str, coro: Any, url: str) -> AccessResult:
826:     """Run one fetch-backend coroutine under a hard wall-clock bound.
827: 
828:     Returns within PG_BACKEND_FETCH_TIMEOUT + PG_BACKEND_CLEANUP_GRACE
829:     regardless of whether `coro` ever finishes — `asyncio.wait` returns after
830:     its timeout unconditionally (unlike `asyncio.wait_for`, which awaits the
831:     cancelled coroutine's cleanup). A backend whose cancellation cleanup itself
832:     exceeds the grace window is detached (post-artifacts teardown — see #552).
833:     """
834:     timeout = _backend_fetch_timeout()
835:     grace = _backend_cleanup_grace()
836:     task = asyncio.ensure_future(coro)
837:     done, _pending = await asyncio.wait({task}, timeout=timeout)
838:     if task in done:
839:         exc = task.exception()
840:         if exc is not None:
841:             return _backend_failure(label, url, f"{type(exc).__name__}: {exc}")
842:         return task.result()
843:     # Timed out — cancel, then allow a BOUNDED grace window for cleanup.
844:     task.cancel()
845:     done, _pending = await asyncio.wait({task}, timeout=grace)
846:     if task in done:
847:         if not task.cancelled():
848:             try:
849:                 task.exception()  # retrieve, discard
850:             except Exception:  # noqa: BLE001
851:                 pass
852:         logger.warning(
853:             "[ACCESS] backend %s exceeded %.0fs wall-clock for %s — cancelled",
854:             label, timeout, _safe_log_str(url, 60),
855:         )
856:     else:
857:         # Cleanup itself exceeded the grace window: detach (ref-kept,
858:         # exception-drained). Residual asyncio.run-teardown case: #552.
859:         _DETACHED_BACKEND_TASKS.add(task)
860:         task.add_done_callback(_drain_detached)
861:         logger.warning(
862:             "[ACCESS] backend %s exceeded %.0fs + %.0fs grace for %s — "
863:             "detached (see #552)", label, timeout, grace, _safe_log_str(url, 60),
864:         )
865:     return _backend_failure(label, url, f"backend_timeout_{timeout:.0f}s")
866:

869:     """
870:     Research access manager.
871: 
872:     Provides multiple methods to access research content.
873:     """
874: 
875:     def __init__(
876:         self,
877:         respect_robots_txt: bool = False,  # For research indexing
878:         use_archive_org: bool = True,
879:         institutional_proxy: Optional[str] = None,
880:         user_agent: str = "POLARIS Research Bot (academic research)",
881:     ):
882:         self.respect_robots = respect_robots_txt
883:         self.use_archive_org = use_archive_org
884:         self.proxy = institutional_proxy
885:         self.user_agent = user_agent
886: 
887:         # Paywall detection patterns.
888:         # M-23f: Tightened to fix false positives on long article bodies.
889:         # The old patterns used greedy `.*` across arbitrary spans, which
890:         # meant a 50K-char NEJM article saying "the authors had full
891:         # access to the data" (far from any "sign in") would match
892:         # `sign.*in.*to.*access` because regex `.*` spans ~49K chars.
893:         # New patterns use `\s+` / `\s*[.:]?\s*` for tight token adjacency
894:         # and word boundaries. Length-gating in `_detect_paywall`
895:         # further protects long article bodies from the loosest patterns.
896:         self.paywall_patterns_strict = [
897:             # These fire on ANY content length — extremely specific
898:             r"\bpaywall\b",
899:             r"\bpremium\s+content\b",
900:             r"\bunlock\s+(the\s+)?full\s+article\b",
901:             r"\bthis\s+article\s+is\s+available\s+to\s+subscribers\b",
902:             r"\blog\s+in\s+to\s+read\s+this\s+article\b",
903:             r"\bsubscribe\s+to\s+read\s+the\s+full\s+article\b",
904:         ]
905:         self.paywall_patterns_short_only = [
906:             # These fire ONLY when content is short (<2K chars) — the
907:             # bare phrase "members only" or "sign in to access" in a
908:             # 50K article body is almost always incidental.
909:             r"\bsubscribe\s+to\s+read\b",
910:             r"\bsign\s+in\s+to\s+access\b",
911:             r"\bpurchase\s+(this\s+)?article\b",
912:             r"\bmembers\s+only\b",
913:         ]
914:         # Back-compat: tests or callers referencing .paywall_patterns get
915:         # the strict-always list (the safer set).
916:         self.paywall_patterns = self.paywall_patterns_strict

1444:                 "Accept-Encoding": "gzip, deflate",
1445:             },
1446:         ) as c:
1447:             r = c.get(url)
1448:         if r.status_code != 200:
1449:             return "", False, "", "", ""
1450:         ctype = (r.headers.get("content-type", "") or "").lower()
1451:         raw = r.text if "text" in ctype or "html" in ctype or "json" in ctype else ""
1452:         if not raw and r.content:
1453:             raw = r.content.decode("utf-8", errors="ignore")
1454:         # BUG-M-13/M-14: extract title from raw HTML BEFORE stripping
1455:         # (the <title> tag is gone after _strip_html).
1456:         extracted_title = _extract_title_from_content(raw)
1457:         # BUG-M-17: detect article-type from bounded body region.
1458:         body_type = _detect_article_type_from_body(raw)
1459:         # Diff-gate P1-C: capture raw ld+json BEFORE _strip_html removes <script>.
1460:         jsonld = _extract_jsonld_blocks(raw)
1461:         content = _strip_html(raw)[:max_chars]
1462:         return content, bool(content), extracted_title, body_type, jsonld
1463:     except Exception as exc:
1464:         logger.debug(
1465:             "[live_retriever] naive-httpx fetch %r failed: %s", url, exc,
1466:         )
1467:         return "", False, "", "", ""

1470: def _fallback_naive_fetch(
1471:     url: str,
1472:     max_chars: int,
1473:     t0: float,
1474:     primary_reason: str,
1475: ) -> tuple[str, bool, str, str, str]:
1476:     """Run the naive-httpx fallback and record its FINAL outcome (I-meta-007b P2a).
1477: 
1478:     Every content-fetch fallback in :func:`_fetch_content` (AccessBypass
1479:     disabled / unavailable / timed out / raised / produced no result) ends by
1480:     delegating to :func:`_fetch_content_httpx_naive`. The pre-fix code traced
1481:     ``fail``/``timeout`` BEFORE that delegation, so a SUCCESSFUL fallback was
1482:     still recorded as a failure. This helper traces the ACTUAL result instead:
1483: 
1484:     * ``status="ok"`` + real ``bytes_received`` (length of fetched content) when
1485:       the naive fetch returned content,
1486:     * ``status="fail"`` otherwise — carrying ``primary_reason`` (the reason the
1487:       primary path fell back, e.g. ``access_bypass_timeout_90s``) in ``error``
1488:       for diagnostics.
1489: 
1490:     ``backend_used="httpx_naive"`` uniformly because the naive fetcher is what
1491:     actually ran. ``t0`` is the single wall-clock start captured at the top of
1492:     :func:`_fetch_content` so latency reflects total fetch time. Record-only +
1493:     fail-safe (``_trace_tool`` swallows its own errors); returns the naive
1494:     fetcher's tuple unchanged so retrieval behavior is identical to before.
1495:     """
1496:     result = _fetch_content_httpx_naive(url, max_chars)
1497:     content, ok = result[0], result[1]
1498:     _trace_tool(
1499:         "fetch_content",
1500:         target=url,
1501:         status="ok" if ok else "fail",
1502:         latency_ms=(time.time() - t0) * 1000.0,
1503:         backend_used="httpx_naive",
1504:         bytes_received=len(content) if ok else 0,
1505:         error="" if ok else str(primary_reason),
1506:         primary_reason=str(primary_reason),
1507:     )
1508:     return result
1509:

1563:     return _M45_LAST_FETCH_TELEMETRY.pop(url, {})

1566: def refetch_for_extraction_with_diagnostics(

codex
**Findings**

P1: S03 is still vulnerable on the oversized/suspect path. `safe_trafilatura_extract()` skips trafilatura for oversized HTML, but [_strip_html](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/live_retriever.py:1403) immediately calls [_readability_extract](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/live_retriever.py:1368), which also runs lxml via `Document(html).summary(...)`. That violates “prefer regex fallback for oversized/suspect docs” because the same document still enters a libxml2-backed parser. My adversarial probe with `_TRAFILATURA_MAX_HTML_CHARS=10` confirmed `_strip_html` still invoked readability on the oversized body.

P1: S02 does not close/kill the abandoned AccessBypass worker or its browser context when the outer deadline fires. [_fetch_content](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/live_retriever.py:2019) joins the daemon thread, records a leak at [line 2025](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/live_retriever.py:2025), and returns fallback at [line 2039](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/live_retriever.py:2039). The worker keeps running until eventual completion; if it is blocked on [_inflight_sem.acquire()](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/live_retriever.py:1991), it can later acquire a slot and launch a stale browser fetch after the caller already timed out. This bounds concurrency but does not satisfy “CLOSE Crawl4AI/Playwright contexts in a finally even on timeout (no leaked browser subprocess).”

P2: C05 telemetry is only added on the AccessBypass-success path. The naive/direct fallback strips raw HTML in [_fetch_content_httpx_naive](C:/POLARIS/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/live_retriever.py:1461) and returns `bool(content)` without emitting `fetched_200_but_empty_extract`, so AccessBypass-disabled/unavailable/timeout cases can still silently collapse a 200 body into a generic failure.

Verification run:
`python -m pytest -q tests/polaris_graph/test_lane_a_fetch_stability_bb5.py` passed.
`python -m pytest -q tests/polaris_graph/test_fetch_access_bypass_wiring.py tests/polaris_graph/test_table_linearize.py` passed.
These tests do not cover the two P1 production gaps above.
